> ⚠ **Frame count caveat.** The EMPIAR imageset header reports **49 frames/movie**; the
> RELION tutorial walk-through (a curated *subset* used for teaching) states **24 frames** and
> dose/frame 1.277. Use the actual frame count of the movies you import (49 for the full
> EMPIAR-10204 TIFFs). Total dose ≈ frames × 1.277 e⁻/Å² (49 × 1.277 ≈ 62.6 e⁻/Å²; EMD-6840
> lists 70 e⁻/Å² per image at deposit — treat dose/frame 1.277 as authoritative and let total
> follow from the imported frame count).

---

## 1. Import

Import the movies and stamp the optics group.

- Pixel size: **0.885 Å**
- Voltage: **200 kV**
- Spherical aberration (Cs): **1.4 mm**
- Amplitude contrast: **0.1**
- Input = the raw TIFF movies (`*_frameImage.tif`) + gain reference (MRC).

---

## 2. Motion correction

RELION's own implementation (relion_motion_correction), dose-weighted.

- B-factor: **150**
- Number of patches (X, Y): **5, 5**
- Binning factor: **1**
- Dose per frame: **1.277 e⁻/Å²**
- Frames: use the movie's actual frame count (tutorial worked example: 24)
- Gain reference: the EMPIAR gain `K2-gain170629.mrc` (tutorial path placeholder: `Movies/gain.mrc`)
- Do dose-weighting: **Yes**

---

## 3. CTF estimation — CTFFIND-4.1

- FFT box size: **512**
- Minimum resolution: **30 Å**
- Maximum resolution: **5 Å**
- Minimum defocus: **5000 Å**
- Maximum defocus: **50000 Å**
- Defocus step size: **500 Å**
- Amplitude contrast: **0.1** (from Import)

---

## 4. Particle picking — Laplacian-of-Gaussian (LoG) autopick

The tutorial's recommended reference-free first pass.

- Min. diameter for LoG filter: **150 Å**
- Max. diameter for LoG filter: **180 Å**
- Adjust default threshold: **0**
- Upper threshold: **5**
- Shrink factor: 0; Write/Read FOM maps: No

*(Optional template-based refinement pass, if a 2D template set is built later: lowpass
references 20 Å, pixel size in references 3.54 Å, angular sampling 5°; optimization run on a
few micrographs at picking threshold 0.8 / min inter-particle distance 200 Å, then the full
run at picking threshold 0.0 / min inter-particle distance 100 Å.)*

---

## 5. Particle extraction — first pass (downscaled)

- Particle box size: **256** pixels
- Rescaled (binned) size: **64** pixels
- Invert contrast: **Yes**
- Normalize particles: **Yes**
- Diameter of background circle: **200** pixels
- White/black dust removal stddev: **-1** (off)

> Rationale: 64-px boxes are fast for 2D classification, the initial model, and the first 3D
> classification. The data are **re-extracted at full size later** (§9) for high-resolution refinement.

---

## 6. Reference-free 2D class averaging

- Number of classes: **100** (after accumulating particles from all micrographs)
- Mask diameter: **200 Å** *(inherited from the extraction/optimisation settings; the
  tutorial does not restate it on the Class2D page — 200 Å is the standard β-gal value, matching
  the InitialModel/Class3D mask diameter)*
- Iterations: **25** (default; output `run_it025_classes.mrcs`)
- GPU-accelerated (worked example: 4 GPUs, 5 MPI × 6 threads)

Select the good classes (clear secondary-structure / well-defined averages) to carry forward.

---

## 7. De novo 3D initial model — SGD

- Number of classes: **1**
- Mask diameter: **200 Å**
- Symmetry: **C1** (do NOT impose D2 yet — build the de novo model in C1, impose symmetry later)
- SGD iterations: **25 initial / 100 in-between / 25 final**
- SGD tab: leave defaults
- Worked example runtime ~15 min (4 GPUs, 5 MPI × 6 threads)

---

## 8. Unsupervised 3D classification

- Number of classes: **4**
- Mask diameter: **200 Å**
- Symmetry: **C1**
- Regularisation parameter T: **4**
- Number of iterations: **25**
- Initial low-pass filter: **50 Å**
- Limit resolution E-step to: **-1** (off)
- Reference: the SGD initial model from §7
- Sampling tab: defaults

Select the best 3D class; keep those particles for refinement.

---

## 9. Re-extraction (full size) + 3D auto-refinement

Re-extract the selected particles at full resolution before high-res refine.

- Re-extraction particle box size: **360** pixels
- Re-scaled size: **256** pixels
- Pixel size after rescaling: **1.244 Å** (= 0.885 × 360/256)

3D auto-refine:
- Reference map: the chosen 3D class, **low-pass filtered to 50 Å**
- Symmetry: **D2** (now impose β-gal's point group)
- Initial low-pass filter: **50 Å**
- Default angular sampling: **7.5°**; local search sampling on auto-refine: **1.8°**
  *(for very highly symmetric particles the tutorial notes 3.7° / 0.9° as alternatives — not
  used here)*
- Minimum MPI processes: 3

---

## 10. Mask creation + first Postprocess

**Mask creation** (from the refined map):
- Lowpass filter map: **15 Å**
- Initial binarisation threshold: **0.005**
- Extend binary map this many pixels: **0**
- Add a soft-edge of this many pixels: **6**

**Postprocessing:**
- Calibrated pixel size: **1.244 Å**
- Estimate B-factor automatically: **Yes**
- Lowest resolution for auto-B fit: **10 Å**
- Use your own B-factor: **No**
- Perform MTF correction: **No** (or apply the K2 MTF if available)
- Skip FSC-weighting: **No**

This gives the gold-standard FSC-masked resolution and the solvent mask used downstream.

---

## 11. CTF / higher-order aberration refinement

Run as a short ladder, each step consuming the previous output STAR + the postprocess STAR.
Minimum resolution for fits = **30 Å** throughout.

1. **Higher-order aberrations:** estimate beamtilt = Yes, also trefoil = Yes, 4th-order
   aberrations = Yes; CTF fitting = No; anisotropic magnification = No.
2. **Anisotropic magnification:** estimate anisotropic magnification = Yes.
3. **Per-particle defocus:** CTF fitting = Yes, fit defocus = Per-particle, fit astigmatism =
   Per-micrograph, fit B-factor = No, fit phase-shift = No, beamtilt = No, 4th-order = No.

Re-refine (3D auto-refine) after the CTF-refined particles, then re-Postprocess.

---

## 12. Bayesian polishing

Two-stage: **train** sigmas on a subset, then **polish** all particles.

- **Train** (Train optimal parameters = Yes): fraction of Fourier pixels for testing **0.5**,
  use **4000** particles, perform polishing = No. (Worked example: ~1 h 15 m, 16 threads.)
  - Trained sigmas (tutorial result): velocity **0.42 Å/dose**, divergence **1600 Å**,
    acceleration **2.61 Å/dose**.
  - *(Defaults if you skip training: velocity 0.2, divergence 5000, acceleration 2.)*
- **Polish** (Perform particle polishing = Yes): min resolution for B-factor fit **20 Å**,
  max **-1**; first frame 1, last frame -1.

Re-refine the polished particles (3D auto-refine) → re-Postprocess. This is where the map
sharpens toward the deposited resolution.

---

## 13. Local-resolution estimation

RELION local resolution (not ResMap):
- Use ResMap? **No**; Use Relion? **Yes**
- Inputs: one unfiltered half-map + the solvent mask
- Calibrated pixel size: **1.244 Å**
- B-factor: **-30** (also used to produce a locally-filtered, sharpened map)
- Output: `LocalRes/.../relion_locres.mrc`

---

## 14. Checking the handedness

> "It is impossible to determine absolute handedness from a data set without tilting the
> microscopy stage." Inspect the map — if α-helices turn the wrong way, the hand is flipped.

Flip with:
```
relion_image_handler --i PostProcess/.../postprocess.mrc \
  --o PostProcess/.../postprocess_invert.mrc --invert_hand
```
Verify by superimposing on a known β-galactosidase atomic model (tutorial suggests fetching
**PDB 5A1A** into UCSF Chimera). **EMD-6840 is map-only (no PDB deposited with this EMPIAR
entry)** — 5A1A / 5A1A-class models are external references for the hand check only.

---

## Target outcome

- Full dataset: **~2.6 Å** (FSC 0.143), D2 imposed.
- A tractable subset (the agent rollout target): **~3.0 Å** is the realistic ceiling.
- Grade map quality (signal + reference consistency vs EMD-6840); there is no deposited model
  to grade map-to-model against for this entry.
literature.md easy how this structure was actually reconstructed in the associated publication, plus distilled guidance for this run · 9,513 chars
# E. coli β-galactosidase (RELION tutorial specimen, full deposit) — literature review

_How this structure was actually reconstructed in the associated publication / deposit, behind the deposited EMD-6840 map. This is the **literature** layer — a factual account of the real workflow, distinct from the generic tutorial / case-study recipe. The **review** below is provided in the easy and medium variants; the **additional instructions** (after the marker) only in easy._

> Provenance: compiled from the associated publication + the EMDB / EMPIAR deposition metadata, with adversarial verification of every numeric claim against primary sources. A dated snapshot — not maintained.

## How EMD-6840 / EMPIAR-10204 was actually reconstructed

### Provenance and an important caveat about "the authors' workflow"

The deposited structure for this environment is **EMD-6840**, *"The first reconstruction of beta-galactosidase solved by cryoARM200,"* deposited by Kato T, Terahara N, and Namba K (released 2018-08-15), with the matching raw movies at **EMPIAR-10204** ([EMPIAR API](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/api/entry/10204/)). The specimen is *E. coli* β-galactosidase bound to the inhibitor PETG — a ~465 kDa, **D2** homotetramer ([EMD-6840 header](https://files.rcsb.org/pub/emdb/structures/EMD-6840/header/emd-6840.xml)).

There is **no dedicated methods paper** for this deposit. The EMDB citation is listed as unpublished ("First data of beta-galactosidase for validation of the state-of-the-art cryo-EM"), so the only authoritative records of how it was built are (a) the EMD-6840 deposited header and (b) the official RELION 3.1 single-particle tutorial (Scheres lab), which is built on a downsampled subset of this exact dataset, specimen "kindly given… by Takayuki Kato from the Namba group at Osaka university" ([RELION tutorial intro](https://relion.readthedocs.io/en/release-3.1/SPA_tutorial/Introduction.html)). The two are different artifacts and must not be conflated: this **REVIEW layer reports what the deposit header records**; the generic tutorial recipe is the agent's reproduction path and is summarized separately in the additional-instructions layer. Note also that the 2.6 Å / 1.8 Å CRYO ARM papers in IUCrJ (Makino/Saha et al. 2020) used a **different** K3-detector dataset, NOT this one ([PMC7340270](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC7340270/)); and the widely-cited Bartesaghi β-gal study (1.9 Å, Titan Krios, EMPIAR-10061) is also a **different** dataset whose numbers should not be cross-applied ([PMC6129192](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6129192/)).

### Data collection (deposit header)

Movies were collected on a **JEOL CRYO ARM 200** (model JEM-Z200FSC), a 200 kV cold-FEG instrument with an in-column omega energy filter, on a **Gatan K2 IS** (4k × 4k) detector in counting mode, saved as compressed TIFF. Optics: pixel size **0.885 Å**, spherical aberration **Cs = 1.4 mm**, nominal magnification 60,000× (calibrated 56,497×), defocus nominal 0.3–2.0 µm (calibrated 0.248–2.167 µm), and an average exposure of **70.0 e/Å² per image** over a 10 s exposure ([EMD-6840 header](https://files.rcsb.org/pub/emdb/structures/EMD-6840/header/emd-6840.xml)). The **raw EMPIAR-10204** deposit is 1,338 multi-frame TIFF micrographs of **49 frames each** (3710 × 3838 px, 16-bit), 321.4 GB total, with a per-frame dose of **1.277 e/Å²** per the tutorial NOTES ([EMPIAR API](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/api/entry/10204/)). Two numbers are easy to get wrong here: the EMD-6840 header itself reports `number_real_images = 2161` (not the 1,338 movie count from EMPIAR), and its stated 70.0 e/Å²-per-image is **not** a rounding of a 62.6 e/Å² total — the 62.6 figure is a back-calculation (1.277 × 49) and is not in the header.

### Processing as recorded in the deposit (RELION 2.1 + Gctf)

The deposited map was built in **RELION version 2.1** with **Gctf v1.06** for CTF correction ([EMD-6840 header](https://files.rcsb.org/pub/emdb/structures/EMD-6840/header/emd-6840.xml)). No motion-correction software is named in the header. Picking is not itemized. The startup reference was a **prior β-galactosidase map, EMD-4116**. Angle assignment used **PROJECTION MATCHING** at **7.5° angular sampling** with **9216 reference projections**, and the final reconstruction algorithm is **BACK PROJECTION**. The final map applied **D2 symmetry** to **93,975 particle images** (`number_classes_used = 1` in the final reconstruction; a `final_three_d_classification` into **3 classes** is recorded upstream). The reported resolution is **2.6 Å** (`res_type = BY AUTHOR`) by the **FSC 0.143** gold-standard cut-off. The map is **240³ voxels** (≈ 212.4 Å per side at 0.885 Å/voxel). There is **no associated PDB** — EMD-6840 is a map-only deposit, so any grading must be map-based (map-map CC / FSC vs the deposit), consistent with the env's map-not-model stance ([EMD-6840 / PDBe](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/pdbe/entry/emdb/EMD-6840)).

### What the deposit did NOT do (vs. the modern reference recipe)

Because the deposit is a 2017–18 **RELION 2.1** run, it predates RELION 3's specimen-specific high-resolution tools. CTF / higher-order-aberration refinement and **Bayesian polishing** — central to the RELION 3.1 tutorial that re-processes this same raw data — are therefore **tutorial-only refinements, not part of the deposited reconstruction** ([RELION 3.1 tutorial](https://hpc.nih.gov/apps/RELION/relion31_tutorial.pdf)). The deposit used standard RELION 2.1 auto-refine plus 3D classification, initialized from EMD-4116 rather than a de-novo SGD model.

### Resolution context

The full-dataset deposit reaches **2.6 Å** (FSC 0.143) with D2 imposed on 93,975 particles. The RELION tutorial — which runs only a 24-movie subset (~4,000 particles) — reaches only **"just beyond 2.8 Å,"** and is explicitly capped near ~2.5 Å by its box-256 re-extraction (1.244 Å/px); it does not approach 2.6 Å precisely because it is a small subset, not the full dataset ([RELION 3.1 tutorial](https://hpc.nih.gov/apps/RELION/relion31_tutorial.pdf)). This subset-vs-full gap is the single most important thing to keep in mind when comparing any agent rollout against the deposited number.

## Additional instructions (distilled for this run)

Reconstruct this from the EMPIAR-10204 movies in cryosparc-tools, following the RELION 3.1 β-gal tutorial recipe. Target = D2 β-galactosidase map; deposit ceiling 2.6 Å (full data), realistic subset ceiling ~2.8–3.0 Å.

**Import / pixel / gain**
- Import at **0.885 Å/px physical** — these are K2 IS **counting** (not super-res) movies, so there is **no factor-of-2 super-res halving** at import. Optics: 200 kV, Cs 1.4 mm, amplitude contrast 0.1.
- Supply the **gain reference** (MRC, e.g. `K2-gain170629.mrc` / `gain.mrc`) for on-the-fly correction. **No gain rotation, no flip**; single gain, no DM4 conversion. Movies are NOT pre-gain-corrected.
- **Read the actual frame count from the data** — the full EMPIAR set is 49 frames/movie; the tutorial subset is 24. Do not hard-code 49. Dose/frame = 1.277 e/Å²; total = frames × 1.277.

**Motion correction**: dose-weighting ON; binning factor **1** (2 is only for super-res — not this data, so the working pixel stays 0.885 Å); use all frames.

**CTF**: per-micrograph defocus/astigmatism (CTFFIND-equivalent; FFT box ~512).

**Symmetry — the key decision**
- Particle is **D2**. Do NOT build the initial model in D2. Run **ab-initio/SGD in C1**, and run 3D classification in C1, so asymmetric junk separates. Verify the symmetry is visible in the C1 map, **align the symmetry axes** (relion_align_symmetry --sym D2 equivalent), then impose **D2 only at the high-resolution Refine3D stage** — this effectively quadruples the particle count.

**Box sizes (two-stage extraction)**
- First pass: extract **256 px**, rescale to **64 px** (4× downscale → 3.54 Å/px) for fast 2D/initial-model/3D-class.
- High-res pass: **re-extract 360 px**, rescale to **256 px** → **1.244 Å/px** (caps resolution ~2.5 Å, leaves room for CTF refinement). Rescale the reference map to match.

**Particle yield**: tutorial subset yields only a few thousand particles (~4,000). LoG autopick diameters 150–180 Å; mask/particle diameter 200 Å. The **full deposit used 93,975 particles** — don't expect that on a subset.

**High-res refinements (RELION-3 era, tutorial-only)**: after the first D2 refine, run CTF/higher-order-aberration refinement (beamtilt/trefoil/4th-order, anisotropic mag, per-particle defocus) then **Bayesian polishing** (train on ~4,000 particles, B-factor fit min-res 20 Å), then re-refine D2 + re-postprocess on the polished particles. This is where the map sharpens toward target resolution.

**Sharpening / post-processing**: soft solvent mask + **automatic (Rosenthal-Henderson) B-factor** sharpening (lowest-res-for-fit 10 Å) inside the mask; FSC-weighting ON. MTF was applied at import — do **not** re-apply MTF at post-process. A user B = −30 is only for the local-resolution-filtered map, not global sharpening.

**Handedness**: SGD/ab-initio handedness is ambiguous. If the map comes out mirrored (α-helices turning the wrong way), **flip with --invert_hand** before grading — the grading pipeline has a handedness gate, and a mirrored map will fail it.

**What "good" looks like**: a D2-symmetric β-gal map, correct hand, FSC 0.143 self-resolution ~2.8–3.0 Å on a subset (2.6 Å only with the full dataset). Grade map-based (map-map CC / FSC vs EMD-6840) — there is no PDB to grade against.
cryosparc-tools-api.md easy/medium/hard the cryosparc-tools API you drive cryoSPARC with · 2,885 chars
# cryosparc-tools API notes (public; tools.cryosparc.com)

> Shared, dataset-agnostic context file. Staged into `REFS_DIR` for every rollout variant and read by the
> agent at run time. The numbers/parameters specific to a dataset are NOT here — they live in `acquisition.md`
> (the told-facts) and, where provided, the processing `tutorial.md` / `literature.md`.

You operate cryoSPARC by writing Python with the `cryosparc-tools` package (public docs: tools.cryosparc.com).
The connection and a project are already set up — see `working-environment.md` for what is pre-bound. Key API:

- DISCOVER the available job types: `cs.print_job_types()` prints every job type — its category, its builder
  TYPE STRING (the string you pass to create_job), and its GUI title (the names a tutorial uses). You can
  filter by category, e.g. `cs.print_job_types("particle_picking")`. This is how you map a processing step to
  the right job-type string.
- CREATE + wire a job:
      job = cs.create_job(project_uid, workspace, "<type_string>",
                          connections={"<input_group>": (source_job_uid, "<source_output_group>"), ...},
                          params={"<param>": value, ...}, title="...")
  After `job.refresh()`, introspect the job to learn its exact input groups, output groups, and parameters
  (names + current/default values) so you know what to wire and what to set:
      spec = job.model.model_dump()["spec"]
      spec["inputs"].keys()    # input-group names to wire INTO
      spec["outputs"].keys()   # output-group names to wire FROM (and to load)
      spec["params"]           # all parameters with their current values
  You can also set a parameter after creation with `job.set_param(name, value)`. Build jobs in dependency order.
- RUN a job: `job.queue(lane=...)` then `status = job.wait_for_done(timeout=..., error_on_incomplete=False)`
  (returns the status string; if it times out the server keeps running it — poll again, don't block unbounded).
  Compute lanes are `LANE_CPU` and `LANE_GPU`; lightweight / interactive jobs run on the master node with
  `lane=None`. Output row counts: `len(job.load_output("<output_group>"))`.
- INTERACTIVE jobs: some jobs pause in a `"waiting"` state when queued (they expect interactive input) rather
  than completing. Drive such a job headlessly via `job.interact(action, body)` and then finalize it, or
  achieve the equivalent curation programmatically from the relevant outputs — your choice. (A `"waiting"`
  job is not `"completed"`; don't `wait_for_done` on it expecting completion.)
- RESULTS: a finished refinement/volume job carries its resolution + diagnostics in its model, at
  `job.model.model_dump()["spec"]["outputs"]["<group>"]["latest_summary_stats"]` (e.g. gold-standard FSC
  resolutions in Å and the Guinier B-factor). You can also `load_output` any result and read MRC maps off disk.
working-environment.md easy/medium/hard the objects and inspection helpers pre-bound in your namespace · 1,785 chars
# Your working environment

> Shared, dataset-agnostic context file. Staged into `REFS_DIR` for every rollout variant and read by the
> agent at run time. It describes the namespace and helpers you act through; it does NOT contain any
> dataset-specific facts.

You write code through one tool, `run_python(code)`, which executes it in a PERSISTENT Python namespace on the
lab workstation and returns stdout + the value of the last expression + any traceback — so you iterate like a
real coder: write a small block, read the result/error, fix, continue.

Pre-bound (do NOT reconnect or create a project/workspace):

- `cs` — a connected cryosparc-tools client
- `project`, `project_uid`, `project_dir` — the target project (already created)
- `workspace` — a fresh EMPTY workspace; build everything here
- `DATA_DIR` — the dataset directory; the raw movies are under it (see `acquisition.md` for the glob)
- `REFS_DIR` — the directory holding the reference materials staged for this run (this file and the others
  named in your brief). Read them with e.g. `print(open(os.path.join(REFS_DIR, "acquisition.md")).read())`.
- `LANE_CPU` / `LANE_GPU` — the compute lanes to queue jobs onto
- `np`, `os`, `json`, `time`, and `find_job(uid)`

To inspect intermediate results, lab visualization utilities are available and return images you can see:

- `show_class_montage(job)` — 2D class averages, labelled by class index
- `show_picks(job, cut=None)` — pick score distribution + picks drawn on micrographs; pass
  `cut=(ncc, power_min, power_max)` to colour kept vs rejected
- `show_volume(job)` — map orthoslices
- `show_mask_sweep(job)` — mask-threshold sweep on a low-passed map

You may also load any output and plot your own diagnostics. Use whatever you need to make your judgments.
literature.md medium how this structure was actually reconstructed in the associated publication · 6,209 chars
# E. coli β-galactosidase (RELION tutorial specimen, full deposit) — literature review

_How this structure was actually reconstructed in the associated publication / deposit, behind the deposited EMD-6840 map. This is the **literature** layer — a factual account of the real workflow, distinct from the generic tutorial / case-study recipe. The **review** below is provided in the easy and medium variants; the **additional instructions** (after the marker) only in easy._

> Provenance: compiled from the associated publication + the EMDB / EMPIAR deposition metadata, with adversarial verification of every numeric claim against primary sources. A dated snapshot — not maintained.

## How EMD-6840 / EMPIAR-10204 was actually reconstructed

### Provenance and an important caveat about "the authors' workflow"

The deposited structure for this environment is **EMD-6840**, *"The first reconstruction of beta-galactosidase solved by cryoARM200,"* deposited by Kato T, Terahara N, and Namba K (released 2018-08-15), with the matching raw movies at **EMPIAR-10204** ([EMPIAR API](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/api/entry/10204/)). The specimen is *E. coli* β-galactosidase bound to the inhibitor PETG — a ~465 kDa, **D2** homotetramer ([EMD-6840 header](https://files.rcsb.org/pub/emdb/structures/EMD-6840/header/emd-6840.xml)).

There is **no dedicated methods paper** for this deposit. The EMDB citation is listed as unpublished ("First data of beta-galactosidase for validation of the state-of-the-art cryo-EM"), so the only authoritative records of how it was built are (a) the EMD-6840 deposited header and (b) the official RELION 3.1 single-particle tutorial (Scheres lab), which is built on a downsampled subset of this exact dataset, specimen "kindly given… by Takayuki Kato from the Namba group at Osaka university" ([RELION tutorial intro](https://relion.readthedocs.io/en/release-3.1/SPA_tutorial/Introduction.html)). The two are different artifacts and must not be conflated: this **REVIEW layer reports what the deposit header records**; the generic tutorial recipe is the agent's reproduction path and is summarized separately in the additional-instructions layer. Note also that the 2.6 Å / 1.8 Å CRYO ARM papers in IUCrJ (Makino/Saha et al. 2020) used a **different** K3-detector dataset, NOT this one ([PMC7340270](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC7340270/)); and the widely-cited Bartesaghi β-gal study (1.9 Å, Titan Krios, EMPIAR-10061) is also a **different** dataset whose numbers should not be cross-applied ([PMC6129192](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6129192/)).

### Data collection (deposit header)

Movies were collected on a **JEOL CRYO ARM 200** (model JEM-Z200FSC), a 200 kV cold-FEG instrument with an in-column omega energy filter, on a **Gatan K2 IS** (4k × 4k) detector in counting mode, saved as compressed TIFF. Optics: pixel size **0.885 Å**, spherical aberration **Cs = 1.4 mm**, nominal magnification 60,000× (calibrated 56,497×), defocus nominal 0.3–2.0 µm (calibrated 0.248–2.167 µm), and an average exposure of **70.0 e/Å² per image** over a 10 s exposure ([EMD-6840 header](https://files.rcsb.org/pub/emdb/structures/EMD-6840/header/emd-6840.xml)). The **raw EMPIAR-10204** deposit is 1,338 multi-frame TIFF micrographs of **49 frames each** (3710 × 3838 px, 16-bit), 321.4 GB total, with a per-frame dose of **1.277 e/Å²** per the tutorial NOTES ([EMPIAR API](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/api/entry/10204/)). Two numbers are easy to get wrong here: the EMD-6840 header itself reports `number_real_images = 2161` (not the 1,338 movie count from EMPIAR), and its stated 70.0 e/Å²-per-image is **not** a rounding of a 62.6 e/Å² total — the 62.6 figure is a back-calculation (1.277 × 49) and is not in the header.

### Processing as recorded in the deposit (RELION 2.1 + Gctf)

The deposited map was built in **RELION version 2.1** with **Gctf v1.06** for CTF correction ([EMD-6840 header](https://files.rcsb.org/pub/emdb/structures/EMD-6840/header/emd-6840.xml)). No motion-correction software is named in the header. Picking is not itemized. The startup reference was a **prior β-galactosidase map, EMD-4116**. Angle assignment used **PROJECTION MATCHING** at **7.5° angular sampling** with **9216 reference projections**, and the final reconstruction algorithm is **BACK PROJECTION**. The final map applied **D2 symmetry** to **93,975 particle images** (`number_classes_used = 1` in the final reconstruction; a `final_three_d_classification` into **3 classes** is recorded upstream). The reported resolution is **2.6 Å** (`res_type = BY AUTHOR`) by the **FSC 0.143** gold-standard cut-off. The map is **240³ voxels** (≈ 212.4 Å per side at 0.885 Å/voxel). There is **no associated PDB** — EMD-6840 is a map-only deposit, so any grading must be map-based (map-map CC / FSC vs the deposit), consistent with the env's map-not-model stance ([EMD-6840 / PDBe](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/pdbe/entry/emdb/EMD-6840)).

### What the deposit did NOT do (vs. the modern reference recipe)

Because the deposit is a 2017–18 **RELION 2.1** run, it predates RELION 3's specimen-specific high-resolution tools. CTF / higher-order-aberration refinement and **Bayesian polishing** — central to the RELION 3.1 tutorial that re-processes this same raw data — are therefore **tutorial-only refinements, not part of the deposited reconstruction** ([RELION 3.1 tutorial](https://hpc.nih.gov/apps/RELION/relion31_tutorial.pdf)). The deposit used standard RELION 2.1 auto-refine plus 3D classification, initialized from EMD-4116 rather than a de-novo SGD model.

### Resolution context

The full-dataset deposit reaches **2.6 Å** (FSC 0.143) with D2 imposed on 93,975 particles. The RELION tutorial — which runs only a 24-movie subset (~4,000 particles) — reaches only **"just beyond 2.8 Å,"** and is explicitly capped near ~2.5 Å by its box-256 re-extraction (1.244 Å/px); it does not approach 2.6 Å precisely because it is a small subset, not the full dataset ([RELION 3.1 tutorial](https://hpc.nih.gov/apps/RELION/relion31_tutorial.pdf)). This subset-vs-full gap is the single most important thing to keep in mind when comparing any agent rollout against the deposited number.

3. HIV-1 BG505 SOSIP.664.T332N Env trimer + 44m Fab env_bg505_44m

A soluble, cleaved, native-like, heavily glycosylated HIV-1 class-I envelope glycoprotein trimer (BG505.SOSIP.664.T332N gp140) bound by the 44m broadly-neutralizing antibody (one Fab per protomer). This is the pilot-matched biology (Ward-lab-style HIV Env + bnAb) at a modest 200 kV resolution (~4.4 Å). It is hard because the dense glycan shield and heterogeneous Fab occupancy make picking/alignment noisy, and because the symmetry call — impose C3 from the trimer biology vs stay C1 as deposited — is a genuine judgment, not a label.

Identity & target

AccessionsEMPIAR-13456 · EMD-36815 · PDB none

# Acquisition facts — HIV-1 BG505 SOSIP.664.T332N Env trimer + 44m Fab

The facts handed to you for this dataset. Everything else — the workflow, every parameter, and every particle/class/mask curation decision — is yours to make.

- **Raw movies:** files matching `movies/*.mrc` under `DATA_DIR` (*.mrc, Gatan K2 Summit, counting; the EMPIAR-13456 deposit). Check how many are present at import.
- **Pixel size:** 1.17 Å.
- **Accelerating voltage:** 200 kV.
- **Spherical aberration (Cs):** 2.7 mm.
- **Total exposure dose:** 60 e/Å².
- **Frames per movie:** ~20.
- **Specimen:** HIV-1 BG505.SOSIP.664.T332N gp140 Env trimer + 44m bnAb Fab (C1 deposit; C3 assembly). ~140 Å trimer core; ~200–280 Å with three peripheral Fabs (box ~280 Å).
- **Symmetry:** the biological assembly is a C3 homotrimer with one 44m Fab per protomer — decide for yourself what symmetry, if any, to impose during refinement.
tutorial.md easy a step-by-step processing recipe — the cryo-EM methods from the paper in which this structure was published · 10,988 chars
# the cryo-EM methods from the paper in which this structure was published (iScience 2023 STAR Methods (Talos Arctica 200 kV / K2; RELION 3.1 pipeline).)
Source: https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC10462834/

> Note: those are the methods the authors followed (a RELION pipeline) — one documented route, a guiding framework rather than the optimal recipe for a cryoSPARC reconstruction of this data. Use them for orientation, translate the intent into cryosparc-tools, and make your own decisions; the goal is always the best reconstruction this data supports.

# Paper Methods — HIV-1 BG505.SOSIP.664.T332N Env trimer + 44m Fab (EMPIAR-13456 / EMD-36815)

> **Provenance.** Compiled verbatim-where-possible from the published STAR Methods of the source paper
> below, for in-context use by a reconstruction agent. This is a faithful procedure transcription,
> NOT original analysis. Where a number could not be confirmed in a primary source it is marked
> **[UNCONFIRMED]** — do not treat such values as ground truth.
>
> - **Specimen:** HIV-1 BG505.SOSIP.664.T332N gp140 envelope trimer (a soluble, cleaved, native-like,
>   heavily glycosylated class-I fusion glycoprotein) in complex with the broadly neutralizing antibody
>   **44m** (a heavy-chain-matured pediatric bnAb, AIIMS-44), imaged as Fab–trimer complex.
> - **Raw data:** EMPIAR-13456 — multi-frame **MRC** movies, **20 frames** each, **1.17 Å** pixel,
>   **4,916** movies, **9.6 TB**. No gain-reference or defect file is included in the deposit.
> - **Deposited result:** EMD-36815 (cryo-EM map, **~4.4 Å**, point group **C1**). **No fitted PDB model
>   is deposited** (map-only).
> - **Source paper:** Kumar S, Singh S, Chatterjee A, Bajpai P, Sharma S, Katpara S, Lodha R, Dutta S,
>   Luthra K. "Recognition determinants of improved HIV-1 neutralization by a heavy chain matured
>   pediatric antibody." *iScience* 26(9):107579 (2023). DOI **10.1016/j.isci.2023.107579**.
> - **Open-access source URL:** https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC10462834/
> - **bioRxiv preprint:** https://www.biorxiv.org/content/10.1101/2023.01.19.524673
> - **EMPIAR record:** https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/api/entry/13456/ ·
>   **EMDB record:** https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-36815

---

## Biology note (why the symmetry decision is gradeable)

The imaged particle is a glycosylated **class-I HIV-1 Env trimer** (BG505.SOSIP.664.T332N gp140) — a
**C3-symmetric** homotrimer of gp120/gp41 protomers — decorated with **three copies of the 44m Fab**, one
bound per protomer at an equivalent epitope. The *biological assembly* of a fully-occupied complex is
therefore **3-fold (C3) symmetric**, and the authors **imposed C3 during 3D classification/refinement** to
boost the limited number of 200 kV particles to ~4.4 Å.

Crucially, the **deposited map (EMD-36815) is C1** (point group 1). The symmetry decision is thus a genuine
fork an agent must reason about, not read off a label:

- **Impose C3** — valid only if every protomer is fully Fab-occupied and the three asymmetric units are
  truly equivalent; averages the three copies, sharpens the conserved trimer core, and is what the authors
  did to reach 4.4 Å.
- **Stay C1** — the conservative choice the deposit reflects; correct if Fab occupancy is sub-stoichiometric
  or the Fabs are conformationally heterogeneous, where forcing C3 would smear partially-occupied density.

A correct agent should recognize the C3 *option* from the trimeric biology, weigh it against occupancy
heterogeneity, and be able to justify either choice — making symmetry a scored decision rather than a given.
(Contrast T20S, where D7 is dictated by the proteasome's architecture and the tutorial.)

---

## Cryo-EM workflow (verbatim-where-possible)

### 1. Sample preparation / vitrification

> "R1.2/1.3 300 mesh copper grids (Quantifoil) (Electron Microscopy Sciences) were glow discharged at 20mA
> for 90 seconds before cryo-freezing. Three microliters of the SEC purified complex of
> BG505.SOSIP.664.T332N gp140 trimer and 44m bnAb (1.2 mg/ml) was applied onto the freshly glow discharged
> grid, and immediately blotted for 8.5 secs without any blot force just after 10 secs of incubation to
> remove excess solvent in pre-equilibrated chamber of FEI Vitrobot Mark IV plunger. The sample was plunged
> into the liquid ethane just after blotting."

### 2. Data collection

> "Cryo-EM data were collected using 200 kV TalosArctica transmission electron microscope (Thermo
> Scientific) equipped with Gatan K2 Summit Direct Electron Detector. Movies were recorded automatically
> using Latitude-S (DigitalMicrograph - GMS 3.5) at nominal magnification of 45,000x at the effective pixel
> size of 1.17 Å. Micrographs were acquired in counting mode with a total dose of 60 e-/Å2, with an exposure
> time of 8 sec distributed for 20 frames. A total of 3000 movies were acquired for the
> BG505.SOSIP.664.T332N gp140 trimer and 44m bnAbs protein complexes respectively."

### 3. Motion correction + CTF

> "Single-Particle Analysis (SPA) were performed for the acquired cryo-EM movies using the Relion version
> 3.1. At first, drift and gain corrections of the individual movies were performed with MotionCorr2 and
> estimated Contrast transfer function (CTF) parameters using CTFFIND 4.1.13 …"

- Motion correction: **MotionCor2** (paper writes "MotionCorr2"), with drift **and gain** correction.
  (No standalone gain reference is deposited at EMPIAR — see gain note below.)
- CTF estimation: **CTFFIND 4.1.13**.

### 4. Particle picking + 2D classification

> "… The particles from best micrographs were chosen for automated picking using 2D reference in Relion and
> extracted with the box sizes of 280 Å for the BG505.SOSIP.664.T332N gp140 trimer and 44m bnAb complexes.
> After three rounds of rigorous 2D classification good classes with high-resolution features of the complex
> were obtained as 1080743 particles. These well-defined particles were selected for 3D classification with
> C3 symmetry."

- Picking: **2D-reference (template) autopick** in RELION (on the best micrographs).
- Extraction box size: **280 Å**.
- After **three rounds** of 2D classification: **1,080,743 particles** retained.

### 5. 3D classification / refinement / sharpening / resolution

> "To achieve high resolution, all particles belonging to the best classes of the complex was accounted for
> 3D auto-refinement and followed by movie refinement. The sharpening for the 3D auto-refined maps was
> performed with Relion 3.1 and PHENIX. Global resolution of Fourier shell correlation (FSC) was estimated
> at the threshold of 0.143 and the estimation of local resolution were performed with ResMap, using two
> auto-refined half maps."

- 3D classification: **with C3 symmetry** (see Biology note for the C1-deposit caveat).
- 3D **auto-refinement** → **movie refinement** (per-particle polishing).
- Sharpening: **RELION 3.1** and **PHENIX**.
- Global resolution: **~4.4 Å** at **FSC = 0.143**.
- Local resolution: **ResMap**, from the two auto-refined half-maps; reported **3.36 – 3.74 Å**.
- Final particle count in the reconstruction (EMDB): **219,374** particles.

### 6. Model building (map-only deposit — context, not a scored target here)

> "Automated model building was iteratively done with Phenix Real Space Refinement. Only the Env trimer (PDB
> ID: 5aco) was docked with cryo-EM maps using UCSF Chimera 'Fit in map' tool. To build the model for bnAb,
> the query sequences of the Fab was submitted to Swiss-Model and the resultant model was also fitted in the
> EM maps."

> No atomic model is deposited for EMD-36815. Model building above is reported in the paper for
> interpretation; the gradeable target for this rollout is the **map**, not a model.

---

## Notes for the reconstruction agent (cryoSPARC port)

The paper pipeline is **RELION 3.1**; this environment drives **cryoSPARC**. The decisions transfer, the
job names differ. A faithful cryoSPARC analogue of the above:

1. **Import Movies** — gain reference: **none deposited**; movies are K2 counting-mode MRC already
   gain-corrected during collection per the paper ("drift and gain corrections … with MotionCorr2"), so
   import without a gain file unless one is later supplied. Pixel **1.17 Å**, **20 frames**, **200 kV**,
   total dose **60 e⁻/Å²**. **Cs is unconfirmed** — see the Cs note before setting it.
2. **Patch Motion Correction** (≈ MotionCor2) → **Patch CTF Estimation** (≈ CTFFIND 4.1.13).
3. **Template/Blob pick → Extract** (paper box ≈ **280 Å**; pick the cryoSPARC box in pixels accordingly).
4. **2D Classification** (multiple rounds; the paper kept ~1.08 M particles before 3D).
5. **Ab-initio + Heterogeneous/Homogeneous Refinement.** Decide **C1 vs C3** here — the trimer biology
   motivates C3, the deposit is C1; justify the call against Fab occupancy heterogeneity.
6. **Local refinement / sharpening**, then validate global FSC (0.143) and local resolution.

### Gain handling

EMPIAR-13456 deposits **only `.mrc` movies and no gain/defect file** (confirmed by listing both the `data/`
directory and its `data/data2/` subdirectory — no `.dm4`, `.gain`, `.tif`, or defect file present). K2
counting-mode movies are gain-normalized on the detector during acquisition, so a separate gain reference is
typically unnecessary at import. If a downstream step demands one, it must be sourced externally — do **not**
fabricate a gain path.

### File-layout caveat

Movies live directly under `…/13456/data/` as `*.mrc`, AND there is a `…/13456/data/data2/` subdirectory
that also contains `*.mrc` movies. The EMPIAR API reports the imageset `directory` as `data` with **4,916**
images; `data2/` appears to hold the canonical full set. Confirm the exact movie count per directory before
committing a glob (see the config's `gaps`).
literature.md easy how this structure was actually reconstructed in the associated publication, plus distilled guidance for this run · 9,545 chars
# HIV-1 BG505 SOSIP.664.T332N Env trimer + 44m Fab — literature review

_How this structure was actually reconstructed in the associated publication / deposit, behind the deposited EMD-36815 map. This is the **literature** layer — a factual account of the real workflow, distinct from the generic tutorial / case-study recipe. The **review** below is provided in the easy and medium variants; the **additional instructions** (after the marker) only in easy._

> Provenance: compiled from the associated publication + the EMDB / EMPIAR deposition metadata, with adversarial verification of every numeric claim against primary sources. A dated snapshot — not maintained.

## How the authors reconstructed EMD-36815 (Kumar et al., iScience 2023)

This environment is grounded on a single deposited reconstruction: the HIV-1 BG505.SOSIP.664.T332N gp140 Env trimer in complex with the broadly neutralizing antibody **44m** (Fab), solved at **~4.4 Å** and deposited as **EMD-36815** (map only, no fitted PDB model). The raw movies are at **EMPIAR-13456**. The authoritative method description is the STAR Methods of [Kumar et al., *iScience* 26(9):107579, 2023](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC10462834/) (doi:10.1016/j.isci.2023.107579), cross-checked against the [EMDB header](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-36815) and [EMPIAR record](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/api/entry/13456/). What follows is the authors' *actual* workflow and numbers — distinct from any generic tutorial recipe.

**Specimen and acquisition.** The SEC-purified complex (1.2 mg/mL, pH 8.0) was vitrified on a Vitrobot Mark IV and imaged on a 200 kV **Thermo/FEI Talos Arctica** with a **Gatan K2 Summit** direct detector in **counting mode**, via Latitude-S (GMS 3.5). Acquisition was at nominal 45,000× / **effective pixel 1.17 Å**, total dose **60 e⁻/Å²** over an 8 s exposure split into **20 frames** (≈3.0 e⁻/Å²/frame), defocus **0.75–2.25 µm** (defocus range from the EMDB header only). The paper reports "3000 movies … acquired," but EMPIAR-13456 actually deposits **4,916 movies** (9.6 TB, signed-16-bit MRC, 20 frames each) — a real acquired-vs-deposited discrepancy. **Spherical aberration (Cs) is not stated in the paper, EMDB, or EMPIAR** — it is not a deposited value here. No gain-reference or defect file is deposited; the K2 counting-mode movies were already detector-gain-normalized at acquisition.

**Pre-processing.** Single-particle analysis was run in **RELION 3.1**. Drift **and gain** correction used **MotionCor2** (the paper writes "MotionCorr2"); CTF was estimated with **CTFFIND 4.1.13**. A distinctive, author-specific cleaning gate followed: CTF-estimated micrographs were curated in **cisTEM** with a **CTF-fit-resolution threshold of 7 Å**, discarding any micrograph not fitting beyond 7 Å. This is a mixed-software (RELION + cisTEM) micrograph QC step that generic single-package recipes skip.

**Picking, extraction, 2D.** Particles were auto-picked with **2D references (template-based)** in RELION from the best micrographs — i.e. templates bootstrapped from the authors' own 2D classes, not blob picking. The paper states extraction "with the box sizes of 280 Å"; this is almost certainly a **280-pixel** box (= 327.6 Å at 1.17 Å), which matches the **deposited map box exactly (280 × 280 × 280 voxels)** — a 280 Å physical box would be too small to contain a glycosylated trimer+Fab with CTF-delocalization padding. The auto-picked/extracted total is **not reported**. After **three rounds of rigorous 2D classification**, **1,080,743 particles** in good classes were retained — the only explicit per-stage count in the paper.

**3D, symmetry, refinement.** These 1.08 M particles went to **3D classification with C3 symmetry** (number of classes not stated). The best classes were taken to **3D auto-refinement followed by movie refinement** (RELION particle polishing). The deposited reconstruction used **219,374 particles** — a number that appears **only in the EMDB header**, not the paper, reflecting a realistic ~5× culling from post-2D to the final map. **Maps were sharpened with both RELION 3.1 and PHENIX**; no numerical B-factor is reported anywhere, and the EMDB header records no applied B-factor (the deposit's recommended contour is 0.0092). Angle assignment is recorded as **Maximum Likelihood**. **Global resolution ~4.4 Å at FSC = 0.143 (gold-standard, two auto-refined half-maps)**; local resolution by **ResMap**, reported **3.36–3.74 Å**. The pipeline is deliberately basic for the resolution: only movie refinement follows auto-refine — **no per-particle CTF refinement, no Bayesian polishing named as such, no focused/local refinement** of the Fab or epitope.

**The symmetry call (the key gradeable fork).** The biological assembly is a **C3 homotrimer** — one 44m Fab per Env protomer, three total. The paper imposes **C3 only at the named 3D-classification step**; the next sentence (3D auto-refinement → movie refinement) does **not restate the point group**, and the **deposited map EMD-36815 is C1** (`space_group = 1` = P1, no symmetry imposed, no point-group tag in EMDB metadata). So the narrative reads C3 while the deposit is C1, and the final-refinement symmetry is genuinely unstated. Caveat: a C1-labelled MRC can come out of a C3-symmetrized refinement (P1 box is the universal default), so "deposit is C1" is certain but "authors refined in C1" is an inference from silent text. The honest framing: C3 was leaned on to rescue resolution from a sparse, low-contrast 200 kV dataset of a soft, heavily glycosylated, flexible class-I fusion trimer + flexible Fab — and the call between C3 (boosts the conserved trimer core if Fabs are fully occupied) and C1/symmetry-expansion (correct if Fab occupancy is sub-stoichiometric or Fabs flex) is exactly the judgment an agent must reason through, **not read off the deposit's C1 label**.

**Model building (context only).** The authors interpreted the map by docking Env (PDB 5ACO) plus a Swiss-Model Fab and Phenix real-space refinement, but **deposited no atomic model**. The gradeable target is the map.

## Additional instructions (distilled for this run)

Prescriptive guidance for reconstructing EMD-36815 from EMPIAR-13456 movies in cryoSPARC.

**Import / pixel / gain**
- Import Movies at **pixel size 1.17 Å**, **200 kV**, **20 frames**, **total dose 60 e⁻/Å²**. This is **counting mode, NOT super-resolution** — do **not** halve to 0.585 Å. Every primary source (EMDB, EMPIAR, paper) agrees on 1.17 Å and the deposited map confirms it.
- **No gain file** is deposited (EMPIAR has `.mrc` movies only, signed 16-bit). K2 counting-mode movies are detector-gain-normalized at acquisition — import with no gain reference. If a downstream step demands one, it must be sourced externally; do not fabricate a path.
- **Cs is NOT a deposited value.** Set **Cs = 2.7 mm** as the standard Talos Arctica facility default for CTF estimation, but flag it as a facility assumption, never as confirmed ground truth.
- **Confirm the movie count before globbing.** EMPIAR deposits **4,916** movies (use this, not the paper's "3000"); movies live under `data/` and a `data2/` subdirectory — verify the count per directory.

**Pre-processing**
- Patch Motion Correction (≈ MotionCor2) → Patch CTF Estimation (≈ CTFFIND 4.1.13).
- Apply a **micrograph cleanup gate** discarding micrographs whose CTF fit is worse than **~7 Å** (the authors used a hard 7 Å cisTEM cutoff). On a low-contrast 200 kV set this matters.

**Picking / extraction**
- Prefer **template picking** bootstrapped from your own 2D classes (the authors used 2D-reference autopicking, not blob).
- **Extract at 280 pixels** (≈ 327.6 Å) at 1.17 Å/px. This matches the deposited map box exactly (280³ voxels). Treat the paper's "280 Å" as pixels — do not extract a 280 Å (~239 px) box.

**2D / 3D / symmetry**
- Run **multiple (≈3) rounds of 2D classification** — the soft, glycan-fuzzy particles need aggressive cleaning. Target **~1.08 M particles** surviving 2D (the authors' number). Over-retaining toward refinement, or collapsing to a tiny set, both signal a mis-call.
- **Symmetry is the scored decision.** Recognize C3 from the trimeric biology (one Fab per protomer) and use it to consolidate the limited 200 kV particle set during 3D classification/refinement. Justify the *final* imposition explicitly against Fab occupancy / conformational heterogeneity: C3 boosts the conserved trimer core; drop to C1 (or symmetry-expansion + local refinement) if Fab occupancy is sub-stoichiometric or Fabs flex. Do **not** simply read C1 off the deposit and call it settled — and do not blindly force C3.

**Refinement / sharpening / what "good" looks like**
- Ab-initio → homogeneous/non-uniform refinement; a particle-polishing analogue (≈ movie refinement) is in-scope. The deposited pipeline is basic — per-particle CTF refinement, Bayesian polishing, and focused/local refinement were **not** used and are not required to match the deposit.
- **Final map should land ~219k particles, ~4.4 Å at FSC 0.143**, with local resolution roughly **3.4–3.7 Å** in the trimer core. Sharpen with an FSC-auto-estimated B-factor (no numerical B-factor is published — do not hard-code one); the deposit's recommended contour is 0.0092.
- **Good ≈ ~4.4 Å, not better.** This is a soft, heavily glycosylated 200 kV target; reaching ~4.4 Å with a clean C3-consolidated core and a defensible symmetry justification is the target. There is **no deposited atomic model** — grade the map, not a model.
cryosparc-tools-api.md easy/medium/hard the cryosparc-tools API you drive cryoSPARC with · 2,885 chars
# cryosparc-tools API notes (public; tools.cryosparc.com)

> Shared, dataset-agnostic context file. Staged into `REFS_DIR` for every rollout variant and read by the
> agent at run time. The numbers/parameters specific to a dataset are NOT here — they live in `acquisition.md`
> (the told-facts) and, where provided, the processing `tutorial.md` / `literature.md`.

You operate cryoSPARC by writing Python with the `cryosparc-tools` package (public docs: tools.cryosparc.com).
The connection and a project are already set up — see `working-environment.md` for what is pre-bound. Key API:

- DISCOVER the available job types: `cs.print_job_types()` prints every job type — its category, its builder
  TYPE STRING (the string you pass to create_job), and its GUI title (the names a tutorial uses). You can
  filter by category, e.g. `cs.print_job_types("particle_picking")`. This is how you map a processing step to
  the right job-type string.
- CREATE + wire a job:
      job = cs.create_job(project_uid, workspace, "<type_string>",
                          connections={"<input_group>": (source_job_uid, "<source_output_group>"), ...},
                          params={"<param>": value, ...}, title="...")
  After `job.refresh()`, introspect the job to learn its exact input groups, output groups, and parameters
  (names + current/default values) so you know what to wire and what to set:
      spec = job.model.model_dump()["spec"]
      spec["inputs"].keys()    # input-group names to wire INTO
      spec["outputs"].keys()   # output-group names to wire FROM (and to load)
      spec["params"]           # all parameters with their current values
  You can also set a parameter after creation with `job.set_param(name, value)`. Build jobs in dependency order.
- RUN a job: `job.queue(lane=...)` then `status = job.wait_for_done(timeout=..., error_on_incomplete=False)`
  (returns the status string; if it times out the server keeps running it — poll again, don't block unbounded).
  Compute lanes are `LANE_CPU` and `LANE_GPU`; lightweight / interactive jobs run on the master node with
  `lane=None`. Output row counts: `len(job.load_output("<output_group>"))`.
- INTERACTIVE jobs: some jobs pause in a `"waiting"` state when queued (they expect interactive input) rather
  than completing. Drive such a job headlessly via `job.interact(action, body)` and then finalize it, or
  achieve the equivalent curation programmatically from the relevant outputs — your choice. (A `"waiting"`
  job is not `"completed"`; don't `wait_for_done` on it expecting completion.)
- RESULTS: a finished refinement/volume job carries its resolution + diagnostics in its model, at
  `job.model.model_dump()["spec"]["outputs"]["<group>"]["latest_summary_stats"]` (e.g. gold-standard FSC
  resolutions in Å and the Guinier B-factor). You can also `load_output` any result and read MRC maps off disk.
working-environment.md easy/medium/hard the objects and inspection helpers pre-bound in your namespace · 1,785 chars
# Your working environment

> Shared, dataset-agnostic context file. Staged into `REFS_DIR` for every rollout variant and read by the
> agent at run time. It describes the namespace and helpers you act through; it does NOT contain any
> dataset-specific facts.

You write code through one tool, `run_python(code)`, which executes it in a PERSISTENT Python namespace on the
lab workstation and returns stdout + the value of the last expression + any traceback — so you iterate like a
real coder: write a small block, read the result/error, fix, continue.

Pre-bound (do NOT reconnect or create a project/workspace):

- `cs` — a connected cryosparc-tools client
- `project`, `project_uid`, `project_dir` — the target project (already created)
- `workspace` — a fresh EMPTY workspace; build everything here
- `DATA_DIR` — the dataset directory; the raw movies are under it (see `acquisition.md` for the glob)
- `REFS_DIR` — the directory holding the reference materials staged for this run (this file and the others
  named in your brief). Read them with e.g. `print(open(os.path.join(REFS_DIR, "acquisition.md")).read())`.
- `LANE_CPU` / `LANE_GPU` — the compute lanes to queue jobs onto
- `np`, `os`, `json`, `time`, and `find_job(uid)`

To inspect intermediate results, lab visualization utilities are available and return images you can see:

- `show_class_montage(job)` — 2D class averages, labelled by class index
- `show_picks(job, cut=None)` — pick score distribution + picks drawn on micrographs; pass
  `cut=(ncc, power_min, power_max)` to colour kept vs rejected
- `show_volume(job)` — map orthoslices
- `show_mask_sweep(job)` — mask-threshold sweep on a low-passed map

You may also load any output and plot your own diagnostics. Use whatever you need to make your judgments.
literature.md medium how this structure was actually reconstructed in the associated publication · 6,113 chars
# HIV-1 BG505 SOSIP.664.T332N Env trimer + 44m Fab — literature review

_How this structure was actually reconstructed in the associated publication / deposit, behind the deposited EMD-36815 map. This is the **literature** layer — a factual account of the real workflow, distinct from the generic tutorial / case-study recipe. The **review** below is provided in the easy and medium variants; the **additional instructions** (after the marker) only in easy._

> Provenance: compiled from the associated publication + the EMDB / EMPIAR deposition metadata, with adversarial verification of every numeric claim against primary sources. A dated snapshot — not maintained.

## How the authors reconstructed EMD-36815 (Kumar et al., iScience 2023)

This environment is grounded on a single deposited reconstruction: the HIV-1 BG505.SOSIP.664.T332N gp140 Env trimer in complex with the broadly neutralizing antibody **44m** (Fab), solved at **~4.4 Å** and deposited as **EMD-36815** (map only, no fitted PDB model). The raw movies are at **EMPIAR-13456**. The authoritative method description is the STAR Methods of [Kumar et al., *iScience* 26(9):107579, 2023](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC10462834/) (doi:10.1016/j.isci.2023.107579), cross-checked against the [EMDB header](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-36815) and [EMPIAR record](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/api/entry/13456/). What follows is the authors' *actual* workflow and numbers — distinct from any generic tutorial recipe.

**Specimen and acquisition.** The SEC-purified complex (1.2 mg/mL, pH 8.0) was vitrified on a Vitrobot Mark IV and imaged on a 200 kV **Thermo/FEI Talos Arctica** with a **Gatan K2 Summit** direct detector in **counting mode**, via Latitude-S (GMS 3.5). Acquisition was at nominal 45,000× / **effective pixel 1.17 Å**, total dose **60 e⁻/Å²** over an 8 s exposure split into **20 frames** (≈3.0 e⁻/Å²/frame), defocus **0.75–2.25 µm** (defocus range from the EMDB header only). The paper reports "3000 movies … acquired," but EMPIAR-13456 actually deposits **4,916 movies** (9.6 TB, signed-16-bit MRC, 20 frames each) — a real acquired-vs-deposited discrepancy. **Spherical aberration (Cs) is not stated in the paper, EMDB, or EMPIAR** — it is not a deposited value here. No gain-reference or defect file is deposited; the K2 counting-mode movies were already detector-gain-normalized at acquisition.

**Pre-processing.** Single-particle analysis was run in **RELION 3.1**. Drift **and gain** correction used **MotionCor2** (the paper writes "MotionCorr2"); CTF was estimated with **CTFFIND 4.1.13**. A distinctive, author-specific cleaning gate followed: CTF-estimated micrographs were curated in **cisTEM** with a **CTF-fit-resolution threshold of 7 Å**, discarding any micrograph not fitting beyond 7 Å. This is a mixed-software (RELION + cisTEM) micrograph QC step that generic single-package recipes skip.

**Picking, extraction, 2D.** Particles were auto-picked with **2D references (template-based)** in RELION from the best micrographs — i.e. templates bootstrapped from the authors' own 2D classes, not blob picking. The paper states extraction "with the box sizes of 280 Å"; this is almost certainly a **280-pixel** box (= 327.6 Å at 1.17 Å), which matches the **deposited map box exactly (280 × 280 × 280 voxels)** — a 280 Å physical box would be too small to contain a glycosylated trimer+Fab with CTF-delocalization padding. The auto-picked/extracted total is **not reported**. After **three rounds of rigorous 2D classification**, **1,080,743 particles** in good classes were retained — the only explicit per-stage count in the paper.

**3D, symmetry, refinement.** These 1.08 M particles went to **3D classification with C3 symmetry** (number of classes not stated). The best classes were taken to **3D auto-refinement followed by movie refinement** (RELION particle polishing). The deposited reconstruction used **219,374 particles** — a number that appears **only in the EMDB header**, not the paper, reflecting a realistic ~5× culling from post-2D to the final map. **Maps were sharpened with both RELION 3.1 and PHENIX**; no numerical B-factor is reported anywhere, and the EMDB header records no applied B-factor (the deposit's recommended contour is 0.0092). Angle assignment is recorded as **Maximum Likelihood**. **Global resolution ~4.4 Å at FSC = 0.143 (gold-standard, two auto-refined half-maps)**; local resolution by **ResMap**, reported **3.36–3.74 Å**. The pipeline is deliberately basic for the resolution: only movie refinement follows auto-refine — **no per-particle CTF refinement, no Bayesian polishing named as such, no focused/local refinement** of the Fab or epitope.

**The symmetry call (the key gradeable fork).** The biological assembly is a **C3 homotrimer** — one 44m Fab per Env protomer, three total. The paper imposes **C3 only at the named 3D-classification step**; the next sentence (3D auto-refinement → movie refinement) does **not restate the point group**, and the **deposited map EMD-36815 is C1** (`space_group = 1` = P1, no symmetry imposed, no point-group tag in EMDB metadata). So the narrative reads C3 while the deposit is C1, and the final-refinement symmetry is genuinely unstated. Caveat: a C1-labelled MRC can come out of a C3-symmetrized refinement (P1 box is the universal default), so "deposit is C1" is certain but "authors refined in C1" is an inference from silent text. The honest framing: C3 was leaned on to rescue resolution from a sparse, low-contrast 200 kV dataset of a soft, heavily glycosylated, flexible class-I fusion trimer + flexible Fab — and the call between C3 (boosts the conserved trimer core if Fabs are fully occupied) and C1/symmetry-expansion (correct if Fab occupancy is sub-stoichiometric or Fabs flex) is exactly the judgment an agent must reason through, **not read off the deposit's C1 label**.

**Model building (context only).** The authors interpreted the map by docking Env (PDB 5ACO) plus a Swiss-Model Fab and Phenix real-space refinement, but **deposited no atomic model**. The gradeable target is the map.

4. CB1–Gi GPCR signaling complex (membrane, C1) cb1_gi

The human cannabinoid receptor CB1 bound to the agonist MDMB-Fubinaca and coupled to a heterotrimeric Gi protein (Gαi/Gβ/Gγ) with a stabilizing scFv16, by cryo-EM at 3.0 Å. A class-A GPCR signaling complex: a 7-transmembrane receptor in a detergent micelle joined to the G protein heterotrimer. It is hard because the assembly is fully asymmetric (C1), small (~160 Å), low-contrast, surrounded by a disordered micelle, and prone to preferred orientation — the canonical membrane-GPCR reconstruction challenge, and a direct match to our cryosparc-tools action space (its canonical recipe IS a cryoSPARC case study).

Identity & target

AccessionsEMPIAR-10288 · EMD-0339 · 6N4B
SymmetryC1 — C1 throughout (asymmetric GPCR–G-protein heterotrimer; no symmetry to apply). Deposit EMD-0339 / 6N4B is C1. No symmetry-selection decision to grade (contrast T20S D7).
Target resolution~3.0 Å
Specimen size~160 Å (receptor + Gαβγ + micelle + scFv16)
Rollout movies2756 (full deposit · 476.0 GB)
Reference materialdocs/reference/cb1-gi-cryosparc-casestudy.md (cryosparc_case_study) · source
Confidencehigh

Acquisition (import)

Microscope / detectorFEI Titan Krios (300 kV) · Gatan K2 Summit, counting
FormatTIFF
Pixel / kV / Cs0.86 Å · 300 kV · 2.7 mm
Dose / frames50.0 e/Å² · ~40 frames
GainGain ships as Gatan .dm4 (two files, one per session). cryoSPARC CANNOT import .dm4 directly: convert with IMOD dm2mrc, then import with 'Flip gain ref in Y? = Yes'. The Feb-19 gain (CountRef_CB1__00826...) pairs with the Feb-19 movie subset selected here; a defect .txt is also provided. Keep the movie subset within one session so the gain/defect match.

Download (box)

Stage to/shared/data/empiar_10288_cb1_gi
Movie source(data root) · glob CB1__*Feb19*.tif
Import glob / gainmovies/*.tif · gain CountRef_CB1__00826_Feb19_14.19.25.dm4
bin/download-empiar --dataset cb1_gi --list-only   # check selection
bin/download-empiar --dataset cb1_gi --full        # fetch all 2756 movies + gain

Run (box, detached)

PYTHONPATH=src python -m recon_env.run_dataset --dataset cb1_gi --variant <easy|medium|hard> \
    --phase execute --project <UID|title> --per-job-timeout 3600 --wall-budget-min 600

Grading

Deposited mapEMD-0339 map
Grading notesMap-only vs EMD-0339 (3.0 Å); 6N4B available for deferred map-to-model. Watch HANDEDNESS (GPCRs often mirror-flip) and ANISOTROPY/preferred orientation (flat micelle). Subset-ceiling. C1 — no symmetry-selection decision.
Manifestruns/agent/grader/manifests/cb1_gi_easy.json
