# the published cryoSPARC end-to-end case study for this exact dataset (cryoSPARC GPCR workshop case study (CB1 / EMPIAR-10288) + RELION-4.0 benchmark.)
Source: https://umich2023.cryosparc.com/gpcr

> Note: that case study is one documented route to this structure — a guiding framework, not necessarily the optimal recipe for your data and cryoSPARC version. Follow it for orientation, but make your own decisions at every step; the goal is always the best reconstruction this data supports.

# CB1–Gi GPCR Complex — cryoSPARC Reconstruction Procedure (EMPIAR-10288)

> **Provenance.** Reconstruction procedure for the **Cannabinoid Receptor 1 (CB1)–Gi protein
> signaling complex**, compiled verbatim-where-possible for in-context use by a reconstruction
> agent. Faithful to the cited cryoSPARC GPCR case study and supporting sources below; do not
> treat any value as authoritative beyond what the source states.
>
> - **Raw movies (EMPIAR):** EMPIAR-10288 — <https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/entry/10288/>
>   (API: <https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/api/entry/10288/>)
> - **Deposited map (EMDB):** EMD-0339 — <https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/entry/EMD-0339>
>   (API: <https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-0339>)
> - **Atomic model (PDB):** 6N4B — <https://www.rcsb.org/structure/6N4B>
> - **Primary procedure source:** cryoSPARC GPCR workshop case study (UMich 2023) —
>   <https://umich2023.cryosparc.com/gpcr>
> - **Supporting:** cryoSPARC Introductory Tutorial (T20S) —
>   <https://guide.cryosparc.com/processing-data/get-started-with-cryosparc-introductory-tutorial> ·
>   cryoSPARC Live "start to finish" guide — <https://guide.cryosparc.com> ·
>   RELION-4.0 benchmark (Kimanius et al., *Biochem. J.* 2021, uses EMPIAR-10288) ·
>   Structure paper: Krishna Kumar et al., *Cell* 178, 2019 — "Structure of a Signaling
>   Cannabinoid Receptor 1–G Protein Complex" (6N4B / EMD-0339).
>
> **Symmetry: C1** (asymmetric GPCR–G-protein heterotrimer — no symmetry to impose).
> **Target: ~3.0 Å** (deposited EMD-0339 resolution; the abbreviated case-study workflow reaches
> ~3.6 Å, the published map reaches 3.0 Å with the full curation/refinement below).

---

## 0. Acquisition facts (carry into Import Movies)

| Field | Value | Source |
|---|---|---|
| Microscope | FEI Titan Krios, 300 kV | EMD-0339 |
| Detector | Gatan K2 Summit (counting mode) | EMD-0339 |
| Raw pixel size | **0.86 Å/px** | EMPIAR-10288 / EMD-0339 |
| Spherical aberration Cs | **2.7 mm** (Titan Krios standard; GPCR case study uses 2.7) | case study; not explicitly deposited |
| Total dose | **50 e⁻/Å²** (deposited; paper methods state ~58 e⁻/Å² — see note) | EMD-0339 / paper |
| Frames per movie | **40** (deposited movies; paper text says 50 — see note) | EMPIAR-10288 |
| Format | TIFF (LZW), 3838 × 3710, UNSIGNED 16-bit | EMPIAR-10288 |
| # movies | 2756 | EMPIAR-10288 |
| Symmetry | C1 | EMD-0339 |

> **Dose / frame-count note.** EMPIAR/EMDB describe the *deposited* movies as **40 frames** with
> total dose **50 e⁻/Å²**; the structure paper's methods describe acquisition as 50 frames / ~58
> e⁻/Å². The cryoSPARC GPCR case study Import step uses **Total dose = 58 e⁻/Å²**. Prefer the
> **deposited** values (40 frames, 50 e⁻/Å²) for the importer unless reproducing the case study
> exactly, in which case use 58. Either is acceptable for dose-weighting; flag the choice.

---

## 1. Gain reference — the dm4 → mrc gotcha (DO THIS FIRST)

The K2 TIFF movies are **not gain-normalized**; you must supply the gain reference at import.
EMPIAR-10288 ships the gain as a **Gatan `.dm4`** file (two of them, one per acquisition session),
plus a defect file:

- `CountRef_CB1__00000_Feb18_23.26.46.dm4` (Feb-18 session)
- `CountRef_CB1__00826_Feb19_14.19.25.dm4` (Feb-19 session)
- `defects_CB1__00000_Feb18_23.26.46.txt` (camera defect file)

**cryoSPARC cannot import a `.dm4` gain directly** — convert it to MRC first with IMOD's `dm2mrc`:

```bash
# IMOD must be on PATH
dm2mrc CountRef_CB1__00826_Feb19_14.19.25.dm4 CountRef_CB1__00826_Feb19_14.19.25.mrc
```

Then, in **Import Movies**, set the converted `.mrc` as the gain reference. For this K2 TIFF
dataset the case study sets:

- **Flip gain ref & defect file in Y? → Yes**

(Reason: the `.dm4`→`.mrc` conversion / SerialEM TIFF orientation convention leaves the gain
mirrored relative to the movie frames for K2 counting data; a Y-flip aligns them. If motion-corrected
micrographs show streaks or a "checkerboard"/grid pattern, the gain flip is wrong — toggle it.)

> The case study uses the **Feb-19** gain (`CountRef_CB1__00826…`). Strictly, each session's movies
> should be normalized by that session's gain; for the abbreviated workflow a single session's gain is
> applied to the demo subset. If processing the full 2756-movie set, split by session (Feb18 / Feb19)
> and import each with its matching gain, or verify a single gain normalizes both cleanly.

---

## 2. Import Movies

Job: **Import Movies**

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Movies data path | `<data_dir>/CB1__*.tif` |
| Gain reference path | `<data_dir>/CountRef_CB1__00826_Feb19_14.19.25.mrc` (converted from .dm4) |
| Defect file path | `<data_dir>/defects_CB1__00000_Feb18_23.26.46.txt` (optional) |
| Raw pixel size (Å) | **0.86** |
| Accelerating voltage (kV) | **300** |
| Spherical aberration (mm) | **2.7** |
| Total exposure dose (e⁻/Å²) | **58** (case study) — or **50** (deposited; see note §0) |
| Flip gain ref & defect file in Y? | **Yes** |

Sanity check: number of imported movies should equal the number of TIFFs picked up by the glob
(2756 for the full set; smaller for a subset).

---

## 3. Patch Motion Correction (Multi)

Job: **Patch Motion Correction (Multi)**, connect `imported_movies`.

- Run with defaults (the case study runs it on **4 GPUs**, no special parameter changes).
- Dose-weighting uses the total dose from Import (§2).
- Output: dose-weighted, motion-corrected micrographs at 0.86 Å/px.

Inspect a few aligned micrographs: vitreous ice, visible particles, no gain artifacts (if a grid /
checkerboard pattern appears, the §1 gain flip is wrong).

---

## 4. Patch CTF Estimation (Multi)

Job: **Patch CTF Estimation (Multi)**, connect motion-corrected `micrographs`.

- Run with defaults (case study: **4 GPUs**).
- Expect defocus values roughly **−0.7 to −2.5 µm** (paper's collection range).
- Output: per-micrograph CTF estimates.

---

## 5. Exposure / micrograph curation

Job: **Curate Exposures** (a.k.a. Manually/Interactively curate exposures).

- Threshold on **CTF fit resolution** (keep micrographs whose CTF fits to ~≤ the target, e.g.
  reject those fitting worse than ~5–6 Å), **relative ice thickness**, and **estimated defocus**
  (drop extreme/empty defocus and thick-ice micrographs).
- Drop empty / contaminated / drift-heavy exposures.
- This step is the main lever separating the ~3.6 Å abbreviated run from the 3.0 Å deposited map:
  the published reconstruction is aggressive about discarding poor micrographs and (later) poor
  particles. The case study does light curation; for near-deposited resolution, curate harder.

---

## 6. Particle picking

GPCR detergent-micelle/nanodisc particles are small and low-contrast; pick generously, then clean
hard in 2D.

### 6a. Blob Picker (first pass)

Job: **Blob Picker**, connect curated `micrographs`.

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Minimum particle diameter (Å) | **100** |
| Maximum particle diameter (Å) | **150** |
| Use elliptical blob | **Yes** (enabled) |

> Particle diameter context: the CB1–Gi complex is **~160 Å** across (receptor + Gαβγ + the
> detergent micelle/scFv). The 100–150 Å blob range targets the protein core, not the full micelle.

### 6b. Inspect Particle Picks

Job: **Inspect Particle Picks**, connect blob picks + micrographs.

| Threshold | Value |
|---|---|
| NCC score | **≥ 0.20** |
| Local power (Power Score) | **635 – 1045** |

Expected retained particles: **~134,000**.

### 6c. Extract (for 2D / templates)

Job: **Extract From Micrographs**, connect inspected picks.

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Extraction box size (px) | **320** |
| Fourier crop to box size (px) | **180** (downscale for speed in 2D/ab-initio) |
| CPU cores | 36 (case study) |

Box rationale: 320 px × 0.86 Å ≈ 275 Å, comfortably > the ~160 Å particle + micelle + CTF delocalization
margin. Fourier-crop to 180 px (≈ 1.53 Å/px) speeds 2D classification and ab-initio.

### 6d. (Optional) Template Picker — second pass

For a cleaner final particle set, build 2D templates from good classes (§7) and re-pick:

- Job: **Create Templates** from selected good 2D classes (or generate from a low-pass ab-initio volume).
- Job: **Template Picker**, **template particle diameter ≈ 160 Å**, connect curated micrographs.
- Re-run Inspect Picks → Extract (same box 320 / crop 180), then 2D-classify again.
  (The abbreviated case study can stop after the blob pass; the deposited map benefits from a
  template-based re-pick.)

---

## 7. 2D Classification & selection

Job: **2D Classification**, connect extracted particles.

- Number of classes: **50** (cryoSPARC default; raise to ~100 for the larger blob set if many junk
  views).
- Run, then **Select 2D Classes**: keep classes with clear secondary-structure / recognizable GPCR +
  G-protein views (transmembrane helices, the Gα Ras-like + AHD lobes, the detergent micelle ring);
  discard blurry, edge, ice, and pure-micelle classes.
- Abbreviated case study retains **~67,000 particles** after selection.
- Iterate 2D (2–3 rounds) for the deposited-quality particle set.

---

## 8. Ab-initio Reconstruction

Job: **Ab-Initio Reconstruction**, connect selected particles.

- **Symmetry: C1** (do not impose symmetry).
- Number of ab-initio classes: **1** for the clean case-study path; use **2–4** classes to separate
  the well-ordered complex from junk / partial (receptor-only or G-protein-only) particles, which
  then feeds heterogeneous refinement (§9).
- Output: one or more initial 3D volumes + per-class particle assignments.

---

## 9. Heterogeneous Refinement (multi-class cleanup)

Job: **Heterogeneous Refinement**, connect the ab-initio volumes (as multiple references) + particles.

- **Symmetry: C1.**
- Use **2–4 classes** (one good complex reference + decoy/junk references from §8).
- Keep the particles assigned to the high-resolution, complete-complex class; discard the rest.
- This is the key 3D cleanup that removes heterogeneous junk the 2D step missed, pushing toward
  deposited resolution. (The abbreviated case study can skip straight to refinement; the published
  workflow uses 3D classification/heterogeneous cleanup.)

---

## 10. Refinement to the final map

Run refinement on the cleaned, complete-complex particle set. Two paths (case study runs both in
parallel and compares):

### 10a. Homogeneous Refinement
Job: **Homogeneous Refinement**, **C1**, enable **per-particle scale (defocus) minimization** and
**optimize per-group CTF params**. Good baseline map.

### 10b. Non-Uniform Refinement (recommended for membrane proteins)
Job: **Non-Uniform Refinement**, **C1**, enable **per-particle scale minimization**.
Non-uniform regularization is specifically beneficial for **small membrane proteins in
detergent/nanodisc** (suppresses the disordered micelle's low-resolution noise), and is the path
to the highest resolution here.

- (Optional) re-extract the kept particles at the **full box (320 px, 0.86 Å/px, no Fourier crop)**
  before the final NU-Refinement to recover high-frequency information.
- Abbreviated case-study expected resolution: **~3.6 Å**. With full curation + heterogeneous
  cleanup + full-box NU-Refine, target the **deposited ~3.0 Å** (EMD-0339).

### 10c. (Optional) Local refinement / masking
For GPCR–G-protein complexes the receptor and the G-protein can refine to different local
resolutions. A focused **Local Refinement** with a soft mask around the receptor (or around the
Gα Ras-like domain) can sharpen the better-ordered region. Not required to reach the global ~3.0 Å.

---

## 11. Validation / outputs

- **Gold-standard FSC = 0.143** → report global resolution (deposited: 3.0 Å).
- Run an **Orientation Diagnostics** / check the FSC for anisotropy (GPCR datasets often have
  preferred orientation from the flat micelle).
- Compare the final map to **EMD-0339** (map-to-map CC / FSC). Check **handedness** — if the
  refined map is mirror-flipped relative to the deposit, flip hand before comparison.
- Final deposited map: EMD-0339; fitted model: PDB 6N4B.

---

## Quick parameter recap (importer + picker critical values)

| Item | Value |
|---|---|
| Pixel size | 0.86 Å |
| Voltage | 300 kV |
| Cs | 2.7 mm |
| Total dose | 58 e⁻/Å² (case study) / 50 e⁻/Å² (deposited) |
| Frames | 40 (deposited) |
| Gain | `CountRef_CB1__00826_Feb19_14.19.25.dm4` → convert to `.mrc` (dm2mrc), **flip in Y = Yes** |
| Defect file | `defects_CB1__00000_Feb18_23.26.46.txt` |
| Blob diameter | 100–150 Å (elliptical) |
| Inspect picks | NCC ≥ 0.20, power 635–1045 (~134K particles) |
| Extract box | 320 px → Fourier crop 180 px |
| 2D classes | 50 (default); keep ~67K |
| Symmetry | **C1** throughout |
| Ab-initio / het-refine | 1 class (clean) or 2–4 (cleanup) |
| Final refinement | Non-Uniform Refinement, C1, per-particle scale |
| Target resolution | ~3.6 Å (abbreviated) → ~3.0 Å (deposited EMD-0339) |
literature.md easy how this structure was actually reconstructed in the associated publication, plus distilled guidance for this run · 10,395 chars
# CB1–Gi GPCR signaling complex (membrane, C1) — literature review

_How this structure was actually reconstructed in the associated publication / deposit, behind the deposited EMD-0339 / 6N4B map. This is the **literature** layer — a factual account of the real workflow, distinct from the generic tutorial / case-study recipe. The **review** below is provided in the easy and medium variants; the **additional instructions** (after the marker) only in easy._

> Provenance: compiled from the associated publication + the EMDB / EMPIAR deposition metadata, with adversarial verification of every numeric claim against primary sources. A dated snapshot — not maintained.

## How the authors actually reconstructed CB1–Gi (EMD-0339 / PDB 6N4B)

**Important citation correction.** The associated publication is **Krishna Kumar K, Shalev-Benami M, Robertson MJ, et al., "Structure of a Signaling Cannabinoid Receptor 1–G Protein Complex," _Cell_ 176(3):448–458.e12 (2019), doi:10.1016/j.cell.2018.11.040, PMID 30639101 ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/))**. The citation carried in the dataset card (Cell 178(5):1166–1178, doi:10.1016/j.cell.2019.08.011) is a _different_ paper (the CB2–Gi structure) and was independently refuted against EMDB, RCSB, and PMC during verification — use the Cell 176 citation.

The reconstructed assembly is the human cannabinoid receptor CB1 bound to the agonist MDMB-Fubinaca, in complex with heterotrimeric Gi and the stabilizing antibody fragment scFv16 — a fully asymmetric, ~membrane-GPCR-class particle (~160 Å) sitting in a detergent micelle ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/)).

**Data collection.** FEI/Thermo Fisher Titan Krios at 300 kV with a Gatan K2 Summit in **counting** mode, calibrated magnification ×29,000 corresponding to a magnified (physical) pixel of **0.86 Å** ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/); cross-confirmed by EMD-0339 sampling = 0.86 Å/voxel, [EMDB](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-0339)). Because acquisition was counting (not super-resolution), the import pixel size equals the physical pixel — there is no 0.43 Å super-res frame to bin. The paper reports a dose rate of ~5.0 e⁻/Å²/s over a 10.0 s exposure with frames at 0.2 s intervals, yielding **50 frames** and an accumulated dose of **~58 e⁻/Å²**; defocus spanned **−0.7 to −2.5 µm** ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/)). Note the deposition diverges from the paper's own text: the EMDB header lists **50 e⁻/Å²** ([EMDB](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-0339)) and the EMPIAR-10288 movies are deposited as **40 frames** ([EMPIAR](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/entry/10288/)). The raw set is 2,756 TIFF movies (3838×3710, 16-bit LZW, ~476 GB) with the gain shipped as Gatan .dm4 ([EMPIAR](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/entry/10288/)).

**Pre-processing.** Beam-induced motion correction was performed in **MotionCor2** (stated verbatim in the STAR Methods); per-micrograph CTF parameters were estimated with **CTFFIND4**. No Gctf, no per-particle/per-group CTF or defocus refinement, and no Bayesian/RELION particle polishing appear anywhere in the methods ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/)). (Whether the final reconstruction used MotionCor2's dose-weighted sums vs. unweighted sums is not explicitly stated — that attribution is a standard inference, not a quoted fact.)

**Particle curation and classification.** An initial **1,178,914** particle projections were extracted by semi-automated procedures and subjected to reference-free 2D classification in **RELION 2.1.0**, retaining **562,312** projections. Maximum-likelihood 3D classification (RELION) used the µ-opioid receptor map **EMDB-7868 low-pass filtered to 60 Å** as the initial reference; conformationally homogeneous groups accounting for **177,787** particles were selected ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/)). This heavy heterogeneity cleanup — discarding receptor-only, G-protein-only, and partial particles — is the principal lever to high resolution.

**Final refinement and sharpening.** Critically, the final high-resolution refinement was **3D masked refinement in Frealign (within cisTEM)** — **not** RELION and **not** cryoSPARC. RELION did only the 2D/3D classification ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/); cross-checked against [EMDB](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-0339) and [RCSB 6N4B](https://www.rcsb.org/structure/6N4B), which name only PHENIX for the separate atomic-model step). The reconstruction was done in **C1 — no symmetry imposed** (EMDB applied-symmetry point group "C1"; angle assignment by maximum likelihood; [EMDB](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-0339), [RCSB](https://www.rcsb.org/structure/6N4B)). Map sharpening used a **two-regime temperature-factor scheme: −90 Å² and −60 Å²** for the low- and high-resolution ends of the amplitude spectrum, respectively — not a single global B-factor ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/)).

**Resolution and validation.** The final map has a global nominal resolution of **3.0 Å** by gold-standard FSC at the **0.143** criterion ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/); [EMDB](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-0339): 3.0 Å, "FSC 0.143 CUT-OFF," 177,787 images used; [RCSB 6N4B](https://www.rcsb.org/structure/6N4B)). Local resolution was computed in **Bsoft (B-soft)** from the two half-maps, giving **2.7–3.6 Å** across most of the map, with the highest resolution at the Gi core ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/)). The deposited map is a **240³** box at 0.86 Å (~206 Å). Model building was iterative manual building in **Coot** with global real-space refinement in **phenix.real_space_refine**, deposited as PDB 6N4B ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/)).

**Where the authors' workflow diverges from the generic cryoSPARC case study.** The deposited 3.0 Å result did **not** come from the cryoSPARC blob→2D→ab-initio→non-uniform-refine recipe at all. It came from MotionCor2 + CTFFIND4 + RELION 2.1.0 classification + a Frealign/cisTEM final refinement, with aggressive micrograph and particle curation and external sharpening/local-resolution tools. The cryoSPARC GPCR workshop case study ([umich2023.cryosparc.com/gpcr](https://umich2023.cryosparc.com/gpcr)) and the RELION-4.0 benchmark ([Kimanius et al., Biochem. J. 478(24):4169–4185, 2021](https://portlandpress.com/biochemj/article/478/24/4169/230248)) are convenient _reproduction_ paths on the same EMPIAR data — the abbreviated case-study subset reaches ~3.6 Å — but they are tutorial recipes, not the published method. Reaching the deposited resolution depends on the heterogeneity cleanup and on checking preferred orientation from the flat micelle, which a generic single-pass recipe omits.

## Additional instructions (distilled for this run)

Prescriptive guidance for reconstructing CB1–Gi from EMPIAR-10288 raw movies in cryoSPARC. The authors used RELION+Frealign/cisTEM; cryoSPARC is the practical reproduction path (case study: [umich2023.cryosparc.com/gpcr](https://umich2023.cryosparc.com/gpcr)).

**Import Movies — pixel size and gain (do gain first).**
- Set **pixel size = 0.86 Å** (counting mode, physical = import pixel; no super-res, no binning), **300 kV**, **Cs = 2.7 mm** (Titan Krios convention; not in the EMDB header), **dose** = 50 e⁻/Å² (deposited) or 58 (paper/case study) — either is fine for dose-weighting; flag the choice.
- Gain ships as **two Gatan .dm4** files (`CountRef_CB1__00000_Feb18…`, `CountRef_CB1__00826_Feb19…`) plus a defect `.txt`. cryoSPARC cannot read .dm4 — convert each with IMOD `dm2mrc` to MRC first. Set **"Flip gain ref & defect file in Y? = Yes"** (K2/SerialEM TIFF convention). If motion-corrected micrographs show streaks/checkerboard, the flip is wrong — toggle it.
- The two gains key to movie-**number** ranges (00000+ and 00826+), not calendar dates. For a tractable subset, take a contiguous numbered range inside one gain's range so the matching gain applies; the case study uses the `00826` (Feb-19) gain on its demo subset.

**Symmetry — decide C1 and never deviate.** The complex is fully asymmetric (7TM receptor + Gαβγ + scFv16). Use **C1 at ab-initio, heterogeneous, homogeneous, non-uniform, and final refinement**. There is no Cn ambiguity here — unlike a viral capsid or an Env trimer, the only correct answer is C1. Imposing any symmetry corrupts the map.

**Pipeline (cryoSPARC reproduction path).** Patch Motion → Patch CTF → Curate Exposures (curate hard — this is a main lever to ~3.0 Å) → Blob Picker (elliptical, 100–150 Å diameter) → Inspect Picks (NCC ≥ 0.20, power 635–1045, ~134K) → Extract → 2D Classify → Ab-initio (C1) → **Heterogeneous Refinement (C1, 2–4 classes)** to strip receptor-only/G-protein-only/partial particles → **Non-Uniform Refinement (C1, per-particle scale)** (NU-refine specifically helps small detergent-micelle membrane proteins).

**Box size.** Extract at **320 px** (×0.86 Å ≈ 275 Å, comfortably > the ~160 Å particle + micelle + CTF delocalization). Fourier-crop to **180 px** for fast 2D/ab-initio; **re-extract at full 320 px / 0.86 Å (no crop)** before final NU-refinement to recover high frequencies. Deposited map is 240³.

**Expected particle yield.** Authors: 1,178,914 extracted → 562,312 after 2D → **177,787 in the final 3.0 Å map** (EMDB-confirmed). Demo subset (~300 movies): ~134K picks → ~67K after 2D → ~3.6 Å. Yield scales with movie count; do not expect 3.0 Å from a small subset.

**Sharpening.** No single global B-factor is published to copy — the authors used two-regime sharpening (−90/−60 Å²) in Frealign/cisTEM. In cryoSPARC, apply the automatic Guinier-fit B-factor at refinement rather than transplanting a deposited value.

**What "good" looks like.** Global resolution toward ~3.0 Å by gold-standard FSC 0.143; local resolution 2.7–3.6 Å (best at the Gi core). Always check **preferred orientation** (Orientation Diagnostics / FSC anisotropy) — the flat micelle makes this dataset orientation-prone. Compare to **EMD-0339** by map-to-map CC / FSC, and **verify handedness** (flip if mirror-relative to the deposit before comparing). Deposited references: EMD-0339, PDB 6N4B.
cryosparc-tools-api.md easy/medium/hard the cryosparc-tools API you drive cryoSPARC with · 2,885 chars
# cryosparc-tools API notes (public; tools.cryosparc.com)

> Shared, dataset-agnostic context file. Staged into `REFS_DIR` for every rollout variant and read by the
> agent at run time. The numbers/parameters specific to a dataset are NOT here — they live in `acquisition.md`
> (the told-facts) and, where provided, the processing `tutorial.md` / `literature.md`.

You operate cryoSPARC by writing Python with the `cryosparc-tools` package (public docs: tools.cryosparc.com).
The connection and a project are already set up — see `working-environment.md` for what is pre-bound. Key API:

- DISCOVER the available job types: `cs.print_job_types()` prints every job type — its category, its builder
  TYPE STRING (the string you pass to create_job), and its GUI title (the names a tutorial uses). You can
  filter by category, e.g. `cs.print_job_types("particle_picking")`. This is how you map a processing step to
  the right job-type string.
- CREATE + wire a job:
      job = cs.create_job(project_uid, workspace, "<type_string>",
                          connections={"<input_group>": (source_job_uid, "<source_output_group>"), ...},
                          params={"<param>": value, ...}, title="...")
  After `job.refresh()`, introspect the job to learn its exact input groups, output groups, and parameters
  (names + current/default values) so you know what to wire and what to set:
      spec = job.model.model_dump()["spec"]
      spec["inputs"].keys()    # input-group names to wire INTO
      spec["outputs"].keys()   # output-group names to wire FROM (and to load)
      spec["params"]           # all parameters with their current values
  You can also set a parameter after creation with `job.set_param(name, value)`. Build jobs in dependency order.
- RUN a job: `job.queue(lane=...)` then `status = job.wait_for_done(timeout=..., error_on_incomplete=False)`
  (returns the status string; if it times out the server keeps running it — poll again, don't block unbounded).
  Compute lanes are `LANE_CPU` and `LANE_GPU`; lightweight / interactive jobs run on the master node with
  `lane=None`. Output row counts: `len(job.load_output("<output_group>"))`.
- INTERACTIVE jobs: some jobs pause in a `"waiting"` state when queued (they expect interactive input) rather
  than completing. Drive such a job headlessly via `job.interact(action, body)` and then finalize it, or
  achieve the equivalent curation programmatically from the relevant outputs — your choice. (A `"waiting"`
  job is not `"completed"`; don't `wait_for_done` on it expecting completion.)
- RESULTS: a finished refinement/volume job carries its resolution + diagnostics in its model, at
  `job.model.model_dump()["spec"]["outputs"]["<group>"]["latest_summary_stats"]` (e.g. gold-standard FSC
  resolutions in Å and the Guinier B-factor). You can also `load_output` any result and read MRC maps off disk.
working-environment.md easy/medium/hard the objects and inspection helpers pre-bound in your namespace · 1,785 chars
# Your working environment

> Shared, dataset-agnostic context file. Staged into `REFS_DIR` for every rollout variant and read by the
> agent at run time. It describes the namespace and helpers you act through; it does NOT contain any
> dataset-specific facts.

You write code through one tool, `run_python(code)`, which executes it in a PERSISTENT Python namespace on the
lab workstation and returns stdout + the value of the last expression + any traceback — so you iterate like a
real coder: write a small block, read the result/error, fix, continue.

Pre-bound (do NOT reconnect or create a project/workspace):

- `cs` — a connected cryosparc-tools client
- `project`, `project_uid`, `project_dir` — the target project (already created)
- `workspace` — a fresh EMPTY workspace; build everything here
- `DATA_DIR` — the dataset directory; the raw movies are under it (see `acquisition.md` for the glob)
- `REFS_DIR` — the directory holding the reference materials staged for this run (this file and the others
  named in your brief). Read them with e.g. `print(open(os.path.join(REFS_DIR, "acquisition.md")).read())`.
- `LANE_CPU` / `LANE_GPU` — the compute lanes to queue jobs onto
- `np`, `os`, `json`, `time`, and `find_job(uid)`

To inspect intermediate results, lab visualization utilities are available and return images you can see:

- `show_class_montage(job)` — 2D class averages, labelled by class index
- `show_picks(job, cut=None)` — pick score distribution + picks drawn on micrographs; pass
  `cut=(ncc, power_min, power_max)` to colour kept vs rejected
- `show_volume(job)` — map orthoslices
- `show_mask_sweep(job)` — mask-threshold sweep on a low-passed map

You may also load any output and plot your own diagnostics. Use whatever you need to make your judgments.

# CB1–Gi GPCR signaling complex (membrane, C1) — literature review

_How this structure was actually reconstructed in the associated publication / deposit, behind the deposited EMD-0339 / 6N4B map. This is the **literature** layer — a factual account of the real workflow, distinct from the generic tutorial / case-study recipe. The **review** below is provided in the easy and medium variants; the **additional instructions** (after the marker) only in easy._

## How the authors actually reconstructed CB1–Gi (EMD-0339 / PDB 6N4B)

**Important citation correction.** The associated publication is **Krishna Kumar K, Shalev-Benami M, Robertson MJ, et al., "Structure of a Signaling Cannabinoid Receptor 1–G Protein Complex," _Cell_ 176(3):448–458.e12 (2019), doi:10.1016/j.cell.2018.11.040, PMID 30639101 ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/))**. The citation carried in the dataset card (Cell 178(5):1166–1178, doi:10.1016/j.cell.2019.08.011) is a _different_ paper (the CB2–Gi structure) and was independently refuted against EMDB, RCSB, and PMC during verification — use the Cell 176 citation.

The reconstructed assembly is the human cannabinoid receptor CB1 bound to the agonist MDMB-Fubinaca, in complex with heterotrimeric Gi and the stabilizing antibody fragment scFv16 — a fully asymmetric, ~membrane-GPCR-class particle (~160 Å) sitting in a detergent micelle ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/)).

**Data collection.** FEI/Thermo Fisher Titan Krios at 300 kV with a Gatan K2 Summit in **counting** mode, calibrated magnification ×29,000 corresponding to a magnified (physical) pixel of **0.86 Å** ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/); cross-confirmed by EMD-0339 sampling = 0.86 Å/voxel, [EMDB](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-0339)). Because acquisition was counting (not super-resolution), the import pixel size equals the physical pixel — there is no 0.43 Å super-res frame to bin. The paper reports a dose rate of ~5.0 e⁻/Å²/s over a 10.0 s exposure with frames at 0.2 s intervals, yielding **50 frames** and an accumulated dose of **~58 e⁻/Å²**; defocus spanned **−0.7 to −2.5 µm** ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/)). Note the deposition diverges from the paper's own text: the EMDB header lists **50 e⁻/Å²** ([EMDB](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-0339)) and the EMPIAR-10288 movies are deposited as **40 frames** ([EMPIAR](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/entry/10288/)). The raw set is 2,756 TIFF movies (3838×3710, 16-bit LZW, ~476 GB) with the gain shipped as Gatan .dm4 ([EMPIAR](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/entry/10288/)).

**Pre-processing.** Beam-induced motion correction was performed in **MotionCor2** (stated verbatim in the STAR Methods); per-micrograph CTF parameters were estimated with **CTFFIND4**. No Gctf, no per-particle/per-group CTF or defocus refinement, and no Bayesian/RELION particle polishing appear anywhere in the methods ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/)). (Whether the final reconstruction used MotionCor2's dose-weighted sums vs. unweighted sums is not explicitly stated — that attribution is a standard inference, not a quoted fact.)

**Particle curation and classification.** An initial **1,178,914** particle projections were extracted by semi-automated procedures and subjected to reference-free 2D classification in **RELION 2.1.0**, retaining **562,312** projections. Maximum-likelihood 3D classification (RELION) used the µ-opioid receptor map **EMDB-7868 low-pass filtered to 60 Å** as the initial reference; conformationally homogeneous groups accounting for **177,787** particles were selected ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/)). This heavy heterogeneity cleanup — discarding receptor-only, G-protein-only, and partial particles — is the principal lever to high resolution.

**Final refinement and sharpening.** Critically, the final high-resolution refinement was **3D masked refinement in Frealign (within cisTEM)** — **not** RELION and **not** cryoSPARC. RELION did only the 2D/3D classification ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/); cross-checked against [EMDB](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-0339) and [RCSB 6N4B](https://www.rcsb.org/structure/6N4B), which name only PHENIX for the separate atomic-model step). The reconstruction was done in **C1 — no symmetry imposed** (EMDB applied-symmetry point group "C1"; angle assignment by maximum likelihood; [EMDB](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-0339), [RCSB](https://www.rcsb.org/structure/6N4B)). Map sharpening used a **two-regime temperature-factor scheme: −90 Å² and −60 Å²** for the low- and high-resolution ends of the amplitude spectrum, respectively — not a single global B-factor ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/)).

**Resolution and validation.** The final map has a global nominal resolution of **3.0 Å** by gold-standard FSC at the **0.143** criterion ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/); [EMDB](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-0339): 3.0 Å, "FSC 0.143 CUT-OFF," 177,787 images used; [RCSB 6N4B](https://www.rcsb.org/structure/6N4B)). Local resolution was computed in **Bsoft (B-soft)** from the two half-maps, giving **2.7–3.6 Å** across most of the map, with the highest resolution at the Gi core ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/)). The deposited map is a **240³** box at 0.86 Å (~206 Å). Model building was iterative manual building in **Coot** with global real-space refinement in **phenix.real_space_refine**, deposited as PDB 6N4B ([PMC6461403](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC6461403/)).

**Where the authors' workflow diverges from the generic cryoSPARC case study.** The deposited 3.0 Å result did **not** come from the cryoSPARC blob→2D→ab-initio→non-uniform-refine recipe at all. It came from MotionCor2 + CTFFIND4 + RELION 2.1.0 classification + a Frealign/cisTEM final refinement, with aggressive micrograph and particle curation and external sharpening/local-resolution tools. The cryoSPARC GPCR workshop case study ([umich2023.cryosparc.com/gpcr](https://umich2023.cryosparc.com/gpcr)) and the RELION-4.0 benchmark ([Kimanius et al., Biochem. J. 478(24):4169–4185, 2021](https://portlandpress.com/biochemj/article/478/24/4169/230248)) are convenient _reproduction_ paths on the same EMPIAR data — the abbreviated case-study subset reaches ~3.6 Å — but they are tutorial recipes, not the published method. Reaching the deposited resolution depends on the heterogeneity cleanup and on checking preferred orientation from the flat micelle, which a generic single-pass recipe omits.

5. MRGPRX2–Gq GPCR signaling complex (Cortistatin-14 bound) mrgprx2 optional

The human Mas-related GPCR member X2 (MRGPRX2) in its active state: bound to the peptide agonist Cortistatin-14, coupled to a Gs-mini-Gq chimera with Gβγ and a stabilizing scFv. C1 (no symmetry). This is the deepest/hardest case in the suite — the cryoSPARC case study was chosen to demonstrate handling FLEXIBILITY and ligand-pose HETEROGENEITY. Difficulty: a very large dataset (12,299 movies / ~3.8 TB) split across two sessions each with its own gain and dose; a long pipeline (heavy exposure curation, two-stage blob→template picking of ~14M picks down to ~1.6M, iterative junk removal, per-particle curation, global CTF refine, reference-based motion correction, focused TMD local refinement, ligand-pose 3D classification); a small, mobile target.

# Acquisition facts — MRGPRX2–Gq GPCR signaling complex (Cortistatin-14 bound)

The facts handed to you for this dataset. Everything else — the workflow, every parameter, and every particle/class/mask curation decision — is yours to make.

- **Raw movies:** files matching `movies/*.tif` under `DATA_DIR` (*.tif/*.tiff, Gatan K3, counting; the EMPIAR-10853 deposit). Check how many are present at import.
- **Collection sessions:** the movies come from more than one session, each with its own gain reference and total dose — 20210311: movies `20210311_*.tif`, gain `CountRef_20210311_109_000.mrc`, dose 50.74 e/Å²; 20210312: movies `20210312_*.tif`, gain `CountRef_20210312_96-1_000.mrc`, dose 47.87 e/Å².
- **Pixel size:** 0.91 Å.  **Voltage:** 200 kV.  **Cs:** 2.7 mm.  **Frames/movie:** ~60.
- **Specimen:** Human MRGPRX2 (class-A GPCR) + Cortistatin-14 + mini-Gq/Gβγ/scFv, C1, ~150 kDa. ~120–160 Å asymmetric complex; 7TM bundle ~40 Å; ~150 kDa.
- **Symmetry (point group):** C1.
tutorial.md easy a step-by-step processing recipe — the published cryoSPARC end-to-end case study for this exact dataset · 14,147 chars
# the published cryoSPARC end-to-end case study for this exact dataset (cryoSPARC case study: end-to-end ligand-bound GPCR (EMPIAR-10853), cryoSPARC v4.7.)
Source: https://guide.cryosparc.com/processing-data/tutorials-and-case-studies/case-study-end-to-end-processing-of-a-ligand-bound-gpcr-empiar-10853

> Note: that case study is one documented route to this structure — a guiding framework, not necessarily the optimal recipe for your data and cryoSPARC version. Follow it for orientation, but make your own decisions at every step; the goal is always the best reconstruction this data supports.

# Case study: End-to-end processing of a ligand-bound GPCR (EMPIAR-10853)

> **Provenance.** Vendored reconstruction procedure for the **MRGPRX2–Gq + Cortistatin-14** GPCR dataset.
> - **EMPIAR:** EMPIAR-10853 (raw movies) · **EMDB:** EMD-24896 (deposited map) · **PDB:** 7S8L
> - **Source (compiled verbatim-where-possible):** cryoSPARC Guide — *"Case study: End-to-end processing of a ligand-bound GPCR (EMPIAR-10853)"*
>   https://guide.cryosparc.com/processing-data/tutorials-and-case-studies/case-study-end-to-end-processing-of-a-ligand-bound-gpcr-empiar-10853
> - **Acquisition cross-refs:** EMPIAR API https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/api/entry/10853/ · EMDB API https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-24896
> - **cryoSPARC version of the case study:** v4.7 · **Deposited resolution:** 2.45 Å (FSC 0.143), C1 (P1).
> - This file is a faithful, condensed transcription of the cited cryoSPARC case study for **in-context use by a reconstruction agent**. Particle counts and parameters are reproduced as written in the source; where the source rounds (e.g. "~11.5M", "~1.6M") this doc preserves the rounding. This is the *deepest / hardest* case in the suite — a flexible, heterogeneous, ligand-bound class-A GPCR signaling complex.

---

## 0. What this dataset is, and why it is hard

The target is the human **Mas-related G-protein coupled receptor member X2 (MRGPRX2)** — a class-A GPCR — captured in its **active, signaling-competent state**: bound to the 14-residue peptide agonist **Cortistatin-14**, coupled to a **Gs-mini-Gq chimera** (mini-Gα), with **Gβγ** subunits and a stabilizing **scFv**. The reconstruction is **C1 (no symmetry)**.

Difficulty drivers (why this is the deepest case in the suite):
- **Flexibility** in the ligand-binding region and **heterogeneity in the ligand-binding pose** — the case study was deliberately chosen to demonstrate strategies for these.
- A **massive raw dataset** (12,299 movies, ~3.8 TB) with **two collection sessions** (2021-03-11 and 2021-03-12), each with its **own gain reference and its own total dose**.
- A long pipeline: heavy curation, two-stage picking (blob → template), iterative junk removal by ab-initio + heterogeneous refinement, particle-quality curation (rebalance orientations + per-particle-scale subsetting), global CTF refinement, **reference-based motion correction (RBMC)**, **local (focused) refinement of the TMD**, and **3D classification of the ligand pose**.
- Final maps are **~2.45–2.83 Å** depending on which ligand-pose class and mask; the single deposited map (EMD-24896) is **2.45 Å**.

---

## 1. Import movies (two exposure groups — one per collection day)

Import the raw movies as **two separate Import Movies jobs**, one per session, because each session has its own gain reference and its own total dose. (Keeping them as separate exposure groups also matters downstream for RBMC.)

Shared parameters:
- **Raw pixel size:** `0.91 Å`
- **Accelerating voltage:** `200 kV`
- **Spherical aberration (Cs):** `2.7 mm`
- **Flip gain reference in Y:** `Yes`

Per-session parameters:

| Session | Movies glob (date prefix) | Gain reference | Total exposure dose |
|---|---|---|---|
| Day 1 — 2021-03-11 | `20210311_*.tif` | `CountRef_20210311_109_000.mrc` | `50.74 e⁻/Å²` |
| Day 2 — 2021-03-12 | `20210312_*.tif` | `CountRef_20210312_96-1_000.mrc` | `47.87 e⁻/Å²` |

Movies are **60-frame** multi-frame TIFFs, `5760 × 4092` px, collected on a **Talos Arctica (G3, 200 keV)** with a **Gatan K3** detector.

---

## 2. Patch Motion Correction (multi)

- Input: both imported movie sets.
- **Output F-crop / format:** 16-bit floating point.
- Parallelize across available GPUs.

## 3. Patch CTF Estimation (multi)

- Default settings, applied to both motion-corrected datasets.

---

## 4. Curate Exposures (manual)

Reject bad exposures using **Manually Curate Exposures** with thresholds:
- **CTF fit resolution upper limit:** `3.5 Å`
- **Average intensity upper limit:** `70`
- **Relative ice thickness upper bound:** `1.042`

**Retained: 11,573 micrographs.**

## 5. Micrograph denoising & junk detection

- **Micrograph Denoiser** — improves particle visibility; the denoised micrographs are used for blob/template picking.
- **Micrograph Junk Detector** — flags extrinsic ice/junk; total junk area is **< 4 %** of the dataset. Junk masks are reused at pick time to reject picks near junk.

---

## 6. Blob picking on a 200-micrograph subset

Pick a small subset first to generate 2D templates.
- Use **Exposure Sets** to take a **200-micrograph** subset.
- **Blob Picker:** min diameter `100 Å`, max diameter `130 Å`.
- **Junk Detector (pass 2)** rejection distance from junk: `30 Å`.
- **Inspect Picks:** NCC threshold `> 0.3`; local power `> -5` and `< 83`.
- Yields **~200k particles** from the 200-mic subset.

## 7. Extract subset + 2D classification → templates

- **Extract:** box `256 px` (233 Å ≈ 2× particle diameter), Fourier-crop to `64 px`, 16-bit float.
- **2D Classification:** `100` classes; max resolution `12 Å`; initial classification uncertainty factor `1`; circular mask diameter `160 Å`, outer `180 Å`; zero-pad factor `1`.
- **Select 2D Classes:** keep classes showing the intact target in side and top views. The selected classes become the **template-picker references**; the *rejected* particle set is later used as a junk reference for heterogeneous refinement.

---

## 8. Template picking (full dataset)

- **Template Picker:** pick on **denoised micrographs** = true; particle diameter `170 Å`; templates = selected 2D classes.
- **Initial picks: ~14 million.**
- **Junk Detector (pass 3)** rejection distance: `30 Å`.
- **Inspect Picks:** same NCC / local-power criteria as the blob picks.

## 9. Extract template-picked particles

- Same extraction as §7: box `256 px`, Fourier-crop to `64 px`, 16-bit float.
- **After filtering: ~11.5 million particles.**

---

## 10. Remove junk via ab-initio + heterogeneous refinement

Build references:
- **Ab-Initio (1):** input = particles **selected** in 2D; `1` class → a clean GPCR-like volume.
- **Ab-Initio (2):** input = particles **excluded** in 2D; `5` classes → junk / poorly-defined volumes.

Iterative cleanup:
- **Heterogeneous Refinement (1):** input = all **~11.5M** extracted particles; references = the ab-initio volumes; refinement box `64` voxels. Best class ≈ **48 %** of particles.
- **Ab-Initio (3):** input = best class of Hetero-Refine 1; `5` classes; "num particles to use" = `20,000`.
- **Heterogeneous Refinements (2–4):** sequential, each keeping the best class(es). Best-class fractions across the rounds: **63 %, 92 %, 95 %.**
- **Result after Hetero 1–4: ~2.3 million particles.**

---

## 11. Re-extract at a larger box

- **Remove Duplicate Particles:** minimum separation `50 Å`.
- **Re-extract:** box `320 px`, Fourier-crop to `256 px` (sampling now ~2.5× particle diameter).

## 12. Non-Uniform Refinement (Refinement 1)

- Minimize over per-particle scale: true.
- Dynamic mask start resolution: `1 Å` (effectively disables dynamic masking early).
- **Result: ~2.9 Å.** Orientation diagnostics: **cFAR = 0.67**, **SCF = 0.826**.

---

## 13. Improve particle-stack quality

- **Rebalance Orientations:** intra-bin exclusion on `alignments3D/alpha`; removes **~300k** particles.
- **(Optional) NU-Refine (Refinement 2):** confirms a **bimodal per-particle-scale** distribution.
- **Subset Particles by Statistic:** subset by **per-particle scale**; split by manual threshold; `1` threshold at `0.9`. Rejects **~400k**; **retains ~1.6 million particles**.
- **NU-Refine (Refinement 3):** input = particles above the `0.9` scale threshold (cluster 1). **cFAR improves 0.67 → 0.76.**

---

## 14. Global CTF refinement → NU-Refine 4

Test two Global CTF Refinement variants against **Homogeneous Reconstruction Only** (mask = `volume.mask_fsc_auto` from Refinement 1):
1. Fit Anisotropic Magnification = true.
2. Fit Anisotropic Mag. + Fit Tetrafoil + Fit Spherical Aberration = all true. **← best.**

- **Local CTF Refinement** (defocus change ≤ `500 Å`) **worsened** resolution slightly → **omitted**.
- **NU-Refine (Refinement 4):** input = particles from Global CTF (variant 2); minimize per-particle scale = true; dynamic mask start `1 Å`; optimize per-group CTF = true; fit tetrafoil = true; fit spherical aberration = true. **Result: ~2.64 Å.**

---

## 15. Reference-Based Motion Correction (RBMC)

Split exposures by collection day into exposure groups, then run RBMC in stages:
- **A & B — Estimate hyper-parameters:** input = particles/volume/mask from Refinement 4; one job per exposure group; final stage = compute empirical dose weights.
- **C & D — Strengthen spatial prior:** clone A & B; override spatial-prior strength to **1/5** of original → better empirical dose-weight plots.
- **E & F — Motion-correct particles:** dose weights from C & D; motion params overridden with A & B values; final stage = motion-correct particles; 16-bit float = true.
- **NU-Refine (Refinement 5):** input = combined particles from RBMC **E** and **F**; settings as Refinement 4. **Map quality and resolution improve** (global FSC reaches ~**2.41 Å** in this branch).

---

## 16. Local (focused) refinement of the TMD

Create a mask around the receptor + ligand:
- Source: **PDB 7S8L chains R (receptor) + A (ligand)**; molmap resolution `20 Å`; resample to the Refinement-5 grid.
- **Volume Tools** mask: threshold (from ChimeraX inspection); dilation radius `3 px`; soft padding `16 px`.

**Local Refinement:** input = volume/particles from Refinement 5; use pose/shift Gaussian priors = true; re-center rotations & shifts each iteration = true; rotation search extent `10°`; shift search extent `5 Å`; initial low-pass `4.5 Å`.
- **Result: 2.69 Å** for the focused (TMD) map (vs ~2.41 Å for the global Refinement 5), with improved TMD density.

> **Simplified-pipeline comparison (case-study §12A).** Omitting the per-particle curation steps (rebalance / scale-subset) leaves ~3M particles and reaches comparable global resolution **but shows radial overfitting artifacts** — the curated ~1.6M-particle stack is cleaner. *Do not* rank purely on resolution.

---

## 17. 3D classification of the ligand-binding pose

Create a **ligand-only** focus mask:
- Source: **PDB 7S8L chain A (ligand only)**; molmap resolution `20 Å`; Volume Tools threshold `0.0063`, type = mask.

**3D Classification:** input = volume/particles from Local Refinement; per-class O-EM batch size `20,000`; O-EM learning-rate init `1`; class similarity `0`; filter resolution `3.5 Å`; `10` classes.
- ESS (mean per-particle class size) ≈ **2.8**; classes roughly **equally populated** → continuous heterogeneity / weak classification signal.
- **Heterogeneous Reconstruction Only** to get a higher-res volume per class; difference maps vs the apo molmap (7S8L chains R/B/C/D/E) reveal ligand density.
- **Manual regrouping** into 4 ligand-shape categories: poorly ordered, partially ordered, linear-ordered, circular-ordered.
- **Homogeneous Reconstruction Only** — one job per ligand-shape category.

---

## 18. Mask optimization for resolution estimation

The auto-tightened FSC mask from Local Refinement includes adjacent G-protein density → make a tighter mask:
- Source: **PDB 7S8L chains R + A**; molmap resolution `15 Å`; resample to the Local-Refinement grid; Volume Tools threshold `0.13` (example), dilation radius `6 px`.
- **Validation (FSC)** of each homo-reconstructed volume against the new mask: **FSC 0.143 resolutions = 2.75–2.83 Å.**

## 19. Sharpening & model building

- **Sharpening Tools:** manually optimized B-factors (e.g. `-50` to `-60`, lower-magnitude than the auto value) to balance receptor side-chain detail vs ligand-density clarity.
- Three ligand models built/refined in Phenix (circular S–S-bonded and linear S–S-broken conformations). A register shift vs the deposited 7S8L was noted.

---

## Particle-count ladder (as written in the source)

| Stage | Count |
|---|---|
| After curation | **11,573 micrographs** |
| Blob picks (200-mic subset) | ~200k |
| Template picks (initial) | **~14M** |
| After template extraction + filtering | **~11.5M** |
| After Hetero-Refine 1–4 | **~2.3M** |
| After Rebalance Orientations | ~2.0M |
| After per-particle-scale subset (`>0.9`) | **~1.6M** |
| RBMC output (combined) → Local Refine input | **~1.6M** |

## Resolution ladder

| Stage | Resolution |
|---|---|
| NU-Refine 1 (64-vox box) | ~2.9 Å (cFAR 0.67, SCF 0.826) |
| NU-Refine 3 (after curation) | ~2.9 Å (cFAR → 0.76) |
| NU-Refine 4 (+ Global CTF, tetrafoil+Cs) | ~2.64 Å |
| NU-Refine 5 (+ RBMC) | ~2.41 Å (global) |
| Local Refinement (TMD) | 2.69 Å |
| Per-ligand-class homo-reconstructions (new mask) | 2.75–2.83 Å |
| **Deposited (EMD-24896)** | **2.45 Å (FSC 0.143)** |

---

## Notes for a reconstruction agent

- **Two exposure groups are not optional bookkeeping** — they carry different doses and different gain refs, and RBMC splits on them. Import as two jobs.
- **Gain handling:** flip gain reference in Y = true; each session uses its matching `CountRef_*.mrc`.
- **Symmetry is C1** throughout — do not impose any point group.
- **Resolution is not a sufficient quality signal here** (the simplified 3M-particle branch reaches similar global resolution but overfits); grade the *procedure* (curation, RBMC, focused refinement, ligand classification), not just the final FSC number.
- **Ground truth for grading** = the deposit (EMD-24896 / 7S8L). The case study itself is the *procedure* reference, not an answer key.
literature.md easy how this structure was actually reconstructed in the associated publication, plus distilled guidance for this run · 11,344 chars
# MRGPRX2–Gq GPCR signaling complex (Cortistatin-14 bound) — literature review

_How this structure was actually reconstructed in the associated publication / deposit, behind the deposited EMD-24896 / 7S8L map. This is the **literature** layer — a factual account of the real workflow, distinct from the generic tutorial / case-study recipe. The **review** below is provided in the easy and medium variants; the **additional instructions** (after the marker) only in easy._

> Provenance: compiled from the associated publication + the EMDB / EMPIAR deposition metadata, with adversarial verification of every numeric claim against primary sources. A dated snapshot — not maintained.

_How the human MRGPRX2–Gq + cortistatin-14 signaling complex was actually reconstructed in the associated publication (Cao, Roth et al., Nature 2021;600:170-175, doi:10.1038/s41586-021-04126-6), behind the deposited EMD-24896 map (2.45 Å) and PDB 7S8L model. This is the **literature** layer — a factual account of the authors' real deposited workflow, deliberately distinct from the generic cryoSPARC case study that reprocesses the same raw EMPIAR-10853 movies with newer, heavier machinery. Inline-cited; descriptive, not prescriptive._

## Specimen and why it is hard

The target is the human class-A GPCR **Mas-related G-protein coupled receptor X2 (MRGPRX2)** captured in its active, signaling state: bound to the 14-residue peptide agonist **cortistatin-14**, coupled to a **mini-Gαq**, with **Gβγ** subunits and a stabilizing **scFv16**. It is a **small (~150 kDa), mobile, asymmetric membrane complex** with a flexible receptor TMD and a heterogeneous ligand-binding pose — exactly the regime where a small particle only reaches high resolution through aggressive curation, and where symmetry can offer no help.

## Data collection

Movies were collected on an **FEI/Thermo Fisher Talos Arctica (G3) at 200 kV** with a **Gatan K3 detector (6k × 4k) in counting mode** ([EMD-24896](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/EMD-24896); [Cao et al. 2021, PMC9150435](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/)). The **physical pixel size is 0.91 Å** (the paper's "physical pixel size of 0.91 Å"; deposited map sampling 0.91 Å) at a nominal magnification of **45,000×**. The detector was run in counting, **not** super-resolution mode. Acquisition used **SerialEM with a multishot (beam-image-shift) array** ([Cao et al.](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/)). Each movie was recorded for **~2.7 s as 60 subframes** at a dose rate of **~15 e⁻/pixel/s**, for a total of **~50 e⁻/Å²** per the paper ([Cao et al.](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/)). Mean defocus was **1.2 µm (SD 0.5 µm)** per Extended Data Table 1 (the table row is labelled "Defocus mean (SD)", not a min–max range; [PMC9150435 Table 1](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/table/T1/)).

A subtlety the agent must reason about: the raw data were collected over **two sessions / collection days (2021-03-11 and 2021-03-12)**, each with **its own gain reference and its own total dose — 50.74 and 47.87 e⁻/Å²** ([EMPIAR-10853](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/EMPIAR-10853/)). The EMDB header records a single aggregated **45.0 e⁻/Å²** per image, a deposition rounding distinct from the paper's ~50 and from the two per-session totals ([emd-24896 header](https://files.wwpdb.org/pub/emdb/structures/EMD-24896/header/emd-24896.xml)). The raw deposition is **12,299 TIFF movies, 60 frames, 5760 × 4092 px, 0.91 Å, ~3.6 TB** ([EMPIAR-10853](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/EMPIAR-10853/)). Cs is the standard Talos Arctica **2.7 mm**.

## Processing pipeline — as published by the authors

The authors' deposited workflow is comparatively **standard, single-consensus cryoSPARC single-particle analysis**, all in C1. Following manual curation, micrographs underwent **cryoSPARC patch-based motion correction and patch-based CTF estimation** ([Cao et al.](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/)). The paper reports **no separate MotionCor2 step and no RELION Bayesian polishing** for this complex (the words "MotionCor2", "polish", "reference-based motion" do not appear). Dose-weighting is the cryoSPARC patch-motion default rather than an explicitly stated step.

Particle picking was **two-stage then neural**: the **Blob picker** picked first; **initial 2D classification of those blob picks generated the templates** for template picking; a **subset of selected particles trained Topaz**, and the micrographs were **re-picked with Topaz** ([Cao et al.](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/)). This funnel began at **3,478,202 initial particle images** (Extended Data Table 1, MRGPRX2-Gq cortistatin-14 column). **2D classification** was used both to clean picks and to seed the templates; no per-class counts are reported. **Multiple rounds of multi-reference (heterogeneous) refinement** in cryoSPARC then resolved the final clean stack — the paper states no explicit ab-initio class counts ([Cao et al.](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/)).

Final reconstruction was in **cryoSPARC**, with **Global CTF refinement** applied before post-processing; CTF correction is recorded by the PDB as **phase flipping and amplitude correction** ([RCSB 7S8L](https://data.rcsb.org/rest/v1/core/entry/7S8L)). The model was refined in **PHENIX** ([RCSB 7S8L](https://data.rcsb.org/rest/v1/core/entry/7S8L)). Notably, **no local CTF refinement** and **no focused/local refinement** are reported for this particular complex in the paper — a receptor-only local refinement is described only for the separate MRGPRX4 structure ([Cao et al.](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/)).

## Symmetry, result, and sharpening

The reconstruction is **C1 — no symmetry imposed** (EMDB space_group 1; PDB 7S8L space group "P 1", Int_Tables 1, reconstruction symmetry_type POINT). There is **no C-vs-higher-symmetry decision here**: the heterocomplex is an asymmetric single copy, so every refinement runs in C1. The symmetry-adjacent challenge is instead the **flexible, mobile receptor TMD** — which the authors' deposit handles via consensus refinement (the case study later adds focused local refinement), not symmetry ([EMD-24896](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-24896)). The starting model was **ab-initio (no external initial model)** ([emd-24896 header](https://files.wwpdb.org/pub/emdb/structures/EMD-24896/header/emd-24896.xml)).

The final map (EMD-24896) used **2,029,927 particles** to reach **2.45 Å at the gold-standard FSC = 0.143 criterion**, in a **256³** voxel box at 0.91 Å ([EMD-24896](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/EMD-24896)). The deposited map was **sharpened with a B-factor of −89.8 Å²** in cryoSPARC post-processing, with alternative **deepEMhancer** post-sharpening of the two half-maps ([Cao et al.](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/)).

## What distinguishes the authors' workflow from the case study

The published recipe is solid but plain: SerialEM multishot → patch motion + patch CTF → blob-seeded templates then Topaz → iterative 2D/3D heterogeneous refinement in C1 → consensus refinement + Global CTF refinement → −89.8 Å² sharpening, landing **2.03 M particles at 2.45 Å**. The official **cryoSPARC case study** (v4.7) layers on machinery the 2021 authors did **not** use — Micrograph Denoiser + Junk Detector, per-particle-scale subsetting, **Reference-Based Motion Correction per exposure group**, explicit **focused 3D classification of the ligand pocket (10 classes)** resolving four cortistatin-14 binding poses, and milder manual sharpening (−50 to −60 Å²) ([cryoSPARC case study](https://guide.cryosparc.com/processing-data/tutorials-and-case-studies/case-study-end-to-end-processing-of-a-ligand-bound-gpcr-empiar-10853)). That reprocessing is a modernized reference, **not** the authors' deposited path — resolution alone does not certify a faithful reproduction.

## Additional instructions (distilled for this run)

Prescriptive defaults for reconstructing **MRGPRX2–Gq + cortistatin-14 from the raw EMPIAR-10853 movies in cryoSPARC**, distilled from Cao et al. 2021, the deposit metadata, and the cryoSPARC case study. The science (C1; a small ~150 kDa flexible membrane complex; a heterogeneous ligand pose) is *given* — it is not to be discovered by trial.

**Import — pixel size and optics**
- Import at the **physical pixel size 0.91 Å directly**. The K3 ran in **counting** mode, NOT super-resolution: EMPIAR movies are 5760 × 4092 px (a super-res movie would be ~11520 × 8184) and the gain is named `CountRef_*` (counted), not `SuperRef_*`. Do **NOT** apply a Fourier-crop / bin-by-2 super-res-to-physical step at import.
- Set **200 kV** and **Cs 2.7 mm**. Any binning later is downstream particle-box Fourier-cropping for speed, not a sensor conversion.

**Two sessions, two gain refs, two doses — the key import decision**
- Import the two collection days as **TWO SEPARATE Import Movies jobs / exposure groups**:
  - Day 1 `20210311_*.tif` → gain `CountRef_20210311_109_000.mrc`, total dose **50.74 e⁻/Å²**.
  - Day 2 `20210312_*.tif` → gain `CountRef_20210312_96-1_000.mrc`, total dose **47.87 e⁻/Å²**.
- Use **"Flip gain reference in Y? = Yes"**. The gains are already MRC — **no .dm4 conversion needed**.
- Using one gain for both days, or merging the doses to a single value, is **wrong**. Keeping two exposure groups also matters if you later run RBMC per group.

**Symmetry**
- Run **everything in C1 — no symmetry to impose**. This is an asymmetric single-copy heterocomplex; there is no C/D/icosahedral question. Do not enforce symmetry in ab-initio or refinement.
- The real challenge is the **flexible receptor TMD / ligand-pose heterogeneity** — address with **focused local refinement using a mask** (and optionally focused 3D classification of the ligand pocket), not symmetry.

**Expected particle yield (heavy attrition is correct)**
- Authors' funnel: **~3,478,202 picked → 2,029,927 in the final consensus map**.
- Case-study reproduction (orientation): blob ~200k on a 200-mic subset → template/Topaz ~14M raw → ~11.5M extracted → ~2.3M after heterogeneous refinement → ~1.6M consensus after duplicate removal.
- Target scale: tens of millions of junk-laden picks curated down to **~1.6–2.0 M good particles** from 12,299 movies. A particle this small only reaches 2.45 Å via this aggressive curation.

**Extraction box**
- Extract the final/refinement stack at **320 px (~291 Å)**, Fourier-cropped to **256 px** for refinement.
- For a fast early 2D pass, extract **256 px Fourier-cropped to 64 px**. (Deposited map box = 256³.)

**Sharpening**
- Deposited authors' value: **B = −89.8 Å²**; alternative deepEMhancer on the half-maps.
- For visualizing the weaker/mobile cortistatin-14 ligand density, a **milder manual B of −50 to −60 Å²** is preferred over the auto value.

**What "good" looks like**
- The deposit is **2.45 Å at FSC = 0.143, C1, 2.03 M particles** (EMD-24896). A correct map is **right-handed**, C1, with a resolved 7TM bundle and interpretable ligand density.
- **Do NOT rank a run by resolution alone** — a wrong-handed or under-curated map can still post a plausible number, and the case study explicitly warns that an under-curated ~3M-particle stack shows radial overfitting at comparable global resolution.
cryosparc-tools-api.md easy/medium/hard the cryosparc-tools API you drive cryoSPARC with · 2,885 chars
# cryosparc-tools API notes (public; tools.cryosparc.com)

> Shared, dataset-agnostic context file. Staged into `REFS_DIR` for every rollout variant and read by the
> agent at run time. The numbers/parameters specific to a dataset are NOT here — they live in `acquisition.md`
> (the told-facts) and, where provided, the processing `tutorial.md` / `literature.md`.

You operate cryoSPARC by writing Python with the `cryosparc-tools` package (public docs: tools.cryosparc.com).
The connection and a project are already set up — see `working-environment.md` for what is pre-bound. Key API:

- DISCOVER the available job types: `cs.print_job_types()` prints every job type — its category, its builder
  TYPE STRING (the string you pass to create_job), and its GUI title (the names a tutorial uses). You can
  filter by category, e.g. `cs.print_job_types("particle_picking")`. This is how you map a processing step to
  the right job-type string.
- CREATE + wire a job:
      job = cs.create_job(project_uid, workspace, "<type_string>",
                          connections={"<input_group>": (source_job_uid, "<source_output_group>"), ...},
                          params={"<param>": value, ...}, title="...")
  After `job.refresh()`, introspect the job to learn its exact input groups, output groups, and parameters
  (names + current/default values) so you know what to wire and what to set:
      spec = job.model.model_dump()["spec"]
      spec["inputs"].keys()    # input-group names to wire INTO
      spec["outputs"].keys()   # output-group names to wire FROM (and to load)
      spec["params"]           # all parameters with their current values
  You can also set a parameter after creation with `job.set_param(name, value)`. Build jobs in dependency order.
- RUN a job: `job.queue(lane=...)` then `status = job.wait_for_done(timeout=..., error_on_incomplete=False)`
  (returns the status string; if it times out the server keeps running it — poll again, don't block unbounded).
  Compute lanes are `LANE_CPU` and `LANE_GPU`; lightweight / interactive jobs run on the master node with
  `lane=None`. Output row counts: `len(job.load_output("<output_group>"))`.
- INTERACTIVE jobs: some jobs pause in a `"waiting"` state when queued (they expect interactive input) rather
  than completing. Drive such a job headlessly via `job.interact(action, body)` and then finalize it, or
  achieve the equivalent curation programmatically from the relevant outputs — your choice. (A `"waiting"`
  job is not `"completed"`; don't `wait_for_done` on it expecting completion.)
- RESULTS: a finished refinement/volume job carries its resolution + diagnostics in its model, at
  `job.model.model_dump()["spec"]["outputs"]["<group>"]["latest_summary_stats"]` (e.g. gold-standard FSC
  resolutions in Å and the Guinier B-factor). You can also `load_output` any result and read MRC maps off disk.
working-environment.md easy/medium/hard the objects and inspection helpers pre-bound in your namespace · 1,785 chars
# Your working environment

> Shared, dataset-agnostic context file. Staged into `REFS_DIR` for every rollout variant and read by the
> agent at run time. It describes the namespace and helpers you act through; it does NOT contain any
> dataset-specific facts.

You write code through one tool, `run_python(code)`, which executes it in a PERSISTENT Python namespace on the
lab workstation and returns stdout + the value of the last expression + any traceback — so you iterate like a
real coder: write a small block, read the result/error, fix, continue.

Pre-bound (do NOT reconnect or create a project/workspace):

- `cs` — a connected cryosparc-tools client
- `project`, `project_uid`, `project_dir` — the target project (already created)
- `workspace` — a fresh EMPTY workspace; build everything here
- `DATA_DIR` — the dataset directory; the raw movies are under it (see `acquisition.md` for the glob)
- `REFS_DIR` — the directory holding the reference materials staged for this run (this file and the others
  named in your brief). Read them with e.g. `print(open(os.path.join(REFS_DIR, "acquisition.md")).read())`.
- `LANE_CPU` / `LANE_GPU` — the compute lanes to queue jobs onto
- `np`, `os`, `json`, `time`, and `find_job(uid)`

To inspect intermediate results, lab visualization utilities are available and return images you can see:

- `show_class_montage(job)` — 2D class averages, labelled by class index
- `show_picks(job, cut=None)` — pick score distribution + picks drawn on micrographs; pass
  `cut=(ncc, power_min, power_max)` to colour kept vs rejected
- `show_volume(job)` — map orthoslices
- `show_mask_sweep(job)` — mask-threshold sweep on a low-passed map

You may also load any output and plot your own diagnostics. Use whatever you need to make your judgments.

# MRGPRX2–Gq GPCR signaling complex (Cortistatin-14 bound) — literature review

_How this structure was actually reconstructed in the associated publication / deposit, behind the deposited EMD-24896 / 7S8L map. This is the **literature** layer — a factual account of the real workflow, distinct from the generic tutorial / case-study recipe. The **review** below is provided in the easy and medium variants; the **additional instructions** (after the marker) only in easy._

> Provenance: compiled from the associated publication + the EMDB / EMPIAR deposition metadata, with adversarial verification of every numeric claim against primary sources. A dated snapshot — not maintained.

_How the human MRGPRX2–Gq + cortistatin-14 signaling complex was actually reconstructed in the associated publication (Cao, Roth et al., Nature 2021;600:170-175, doi:10.1038/s41586-021-04126-6), behind the deposited EMD-24896 map (2.45 Å) and PDB 7S8L model. This is the **literature** layer — a factual account of the authors' real deposited workflow, deliberately distinct from the generic cryoSPARC case study that reprocesses the same raw EMPIAR-10853 movies with newer, heavier machinery. Inline-cited; descriptive, not prescriptive._

## Data collection

Movies were collected on an **FEI/Thermo Fisher Talos Arctica (G3) at 200 kV** with a **Gatan K3 detector (6k × 4k) in counting mode** ([EMD-24896](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/EMD-24896); [Cao et al. 2021, PMC9150435](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/)). The **physical pixel size is 0.91 Å** (the paper's "physical pixel size of 0.91 Å"; deposited map sampling 0.91 Å) at a nominal magnification of **45,000×**. The detector was run in counting, **not** super-resolution mode. Acquisition used **SerialEM with a multishot (beam-image-shift) array** ([Cao et al.](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/)). Each movie was recorded for **~2.7 s as 60 subframes** at a dose rate of **~15 e⁻/pixel/s**, for a total of **~50 e⁻/Å²** per the paper ([Cao et al.](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/)). Mean defocus was **1.2 µm (SD 0.5 µm)** per Extended Data Table 1 (the table row is labelled "Defocus mean (SD)", not a min–max range; [PMC9150435 Table 1](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/table/T1/)).

A subtlety the agent must reason about: the raw data were collected over **two sessions / collection days (2021-03-11 and 2021-03-12)**, each with **its own gain reference and its own total dose — 50.74 and 47.87 e⁻/Å²** ([EMPIAR-10853](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/EMPIAR-10853/)). The EMDB header records a single aggregated **45.0 e⁻/Å²** per image, a deposition rounding distinct from the paper's ~50 and from the two per-session totals ([emd-24896 header](https://files.wwpdb.org/pub/emdb/structures/EMD-24896/header/emd-24896.xml)). The raw deposition is **12,299 TIFF movies, 60 frames, 5760 × 4092 px, 0.91 Å, ~3.6 TB** ([EMPIAR-10853](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/EMPIAR-10853/)). Cs is the standard Talos Arctica **2.7 mm**.

## Processing pipeline — as published by the authors

The authors' deposited workflow is comparatively **standard, single-consensus cryoSPARC single-particle analysis**, all in C1. Following manual curation, micrographs underwent **cryoSPARC patch-based motion correction and patch-based CTF estimation** ([Cao et al.](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/)). The paper reports **no separate MotionCor2 step and no RELION Bayesian polishing** for this complex (the words "MotionCor2", "polish", "reference-based motion" do not appear). Dose-weighting is the cryoSPARC patch-motion default rather than an explicitly stated step.

Particle picking was **two-stage then neural**: the **Blob picker** picked first; **initial 2D classification of those blob picks generated the templates** for template picking; a **subset of selected particles trained Topaz**, and the micrographs were **re-picked with Topaz** ([Cao et al.](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/)). This funnel began at **3,478,202 initial particle images** (Extended Data Table 1, MRGPRX2-Gq cortistatin-14 column). **2D classification** was used both to clean picks and to seed the templates; no per-class counts are reported. **Multiple rounds of multi-reference (heterogeneous) refinement** in cryoSPARC then resolved the final clean stack — the paper states no explicit ab-initio class counts ([Cao et al.](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/)).

Final reconstruction was in **cryoSPARC**, with **Global CTF refinement** applied before post-processing; CTF correction is recorded by the PDB as **phase flipping and amplitude correction** ([RCSB 7S8L](https://data.rcsb.org/rest/v1/core/entry/7S8L)). The model was refined in **PHENIX** ([RCSB 7S8L](https://data.rcsb.org/rest/v1/core/entry/7S8L)). Notably, **no local CTF refinement** and **no focused/local refinement** are reported for this particular complex in the paper — a receptor-only local refinement is described only for the separate MRGPRX4 structure ([Cao et al.](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/)).

## Symmetry, result, and sharpening

The reconstruction is **C1 — no symmetry imposed** (EMDB space_group 1; PDB 7S8L space group "P 1", Int_Tables 1, reconstruction symmetry_type POINT). There is **no C-vs-higher-symmetry decision here**: the heterocomplex is an asymmetric single copy, so every refinement runs in C1. The symmetry-adjacent challenge is instead the **flexible, mobile receptor TMD** — which the authors' deposit handles via consensus refinement (the case study later adds focused local refinement), not symmetry ([EMD-24896](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-24896)). The starting model was **ab-initio (no external initial model)** ([emd-24896 header](https://files.wwpdb.org/pub/emdb/structures/EMD-24896/header/emd-24896.xml)).

The final map (EMD-24896) used **2,029,927 particles** to reach **2.45 Å at the gold-standard FSC = 0.143 criterion**, in a **256³** voxel box at 0.91 Å ([EMD-24896](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/EMD-24896)). The deposited map was **sharpened with a B-factor of −89.8 Å²** in cryoSPARC post-processing, with alternative **deepEMhancer** post-sharpening of the two half-maps ([Cao et al.](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9150435/)).

## What distinguishes the authors' workflow from the case study

The published recipe is solid but plain: SerialEM multishot → patch motion + patch CTF → blob-seeded templates then Topaz → iterative 2D/3D heterogeneous refinement in C1 → consensus refinement + Global CTF refinement → −89.8 Å² sharpening, landing **2.03 M particles at 2.45 Å**. The official **cryoSPARC case study** (v4.7) layers on machinery the 2021 authors did **not** use — Micrograph Denoiser + Junk Detector, per-particle-scale subsetting, **Reference-Based Motion Correction per exposure group**, explicit **focused 3D classification of the ligand pocket (10 classes)** resolving four cortistatin-14 binding poses, and milder manual sharpening (−50 to −60 Å²) ([cryoSPARC case study](https://guide.cryosparc.com/processing-data/tutorials-and-case-studies/case-study-end-to-end-processing-of-a-ligand-bound-gpcr-empiar-10853)). That reprocessing is a modernized reference, **not** the authors' deposited path — resolution alone does not certify a faithful reproduction.

6. Encapsulin + ferritin cargo (EMPIAR-10716) — I shell + D5 cargo encapsulin optional

The Haliangium ochraceum encapsulin is a ~24 nm icosahedral (T=1, 60-subunit) protein nanocompartment that packages four encapsulated-ferritin (EncFtn) decamers as cargo. The shell has icosahedral (I) symmetry and refines to 2.5 Å (EMD-12853 / 7ODW); each cargo decamer has D5 symmetry arranged on a tetrahedron. This is the official cryoSPARC case study for UNCONVENTIONAL symmetry: high-symmetry ab-initio, symmetry alignment to I, refinement with symmetry relaxation, shell subtraction, then a CUSTOM non-point-group symmetry expansion over the four cargo positions and D5 local refinement (~2.8 Å cargo). The shell is an easy high-symmetry refinement; the breadth (building the four-position custom expansion) is what makes it hard.

Identity & target

AccessionsEMPIAR-10716 · EMD-12853 · 7ODW
SymmetryI — Two symmetries. SHELL = I: ab-initio in C1 (preserve cargo), align to I (Volume Alignment Tools), Homogeneous Refinement symmetry I + relaxation, then Homogeneous Reconstruction Only (I) = 2.5 Å — the deposited EMD-12853. CARGO = D5 per decamer, recovered only AFTER shell subtraction + a custom non-point-group expansion over four tetrahedral positions + D5 local refinement (no separate EMDB map; procedure-only).
Target resolution~2.5 Å
Specimen size~240 Å (24 nm) icosahedral shell; four internal ~120 Å EncFtn decamers
Rollout movies8109 (full deposit · 1.7 TB (whole deposit))
Reference materialdocs/reference/encapsulin-cryosparc-casestudy.md (cryosparc_case_study) · source
Confidencehigh

Acquisition (import)

Microscope / detectorFEI Titan Krios (300 kV) · Gatan K3, super-resolution counting
FormatTIFF
Pixel / kV / Cs0.652 Å · 300 kV · 2.7 mm
Dose / frames40.509 e/Å² · ~40 frames
GainGain = micrographs/gain.dm4 (~360 MB, DM4) at the micrographs root; cryoSPARC accepts .dm4 directly. Per-image *_gain.tiff files also sit in each Data/ dir — those are EPU acquisition gains, NOT movies; the glob targets *_fractions.tiff so they are excluded. K3 super-res TIFF; F-crop 0.5 to the 0.652 Å working pixel; no defect/EER.

Movies nested under micrographs/GridSquare_*/Data/FoilHole_*_fractions.tiff (recursive); the downloader flattens them into movies/. Cs 2.7 mm from the case study. - **Total exposure dose:** 40.509 e/Å².
- **Frames per movie:** ~40.
