# the published cryoSPARC end-to-end case study for this exact dataset (cryoSPARC case study: end-to-end encapsulated ferritin (EMPIAR-10716).)
Source: https://guide.cryosparc.com/processing-data/tutorials-and-case-studies/case-study-end-to-end-processing-of-encapsulated-ferritin-empiar-10716

> Note: that case study is one documented route to this structure — a guiding framework, not necessarily the optimal recipe for your data and cryoSPARC version. Follow it for orientation, but make your own decisions at every step; the goal is always the best reconstruction this data supports.

# cryoSPARC Case Study — End-to-end processing of encapsulated ferritin (EMPIAR-10716)

> **Provenance.** Compiled verbatim-where-possible from the official cryoSPARC Guide case study
> "Case Study: End-to-end processing of encapsulated ferritin (EMPIAR-10716)" for in-context use by a
> reconstruction agent. This is a faithful procedure transcription, NOT original analysis.
>
> - **Specimen:** *Haliangium ochraceum* encapsulin nanocompartment with four encapsulated ferritin
>   (EncFtn) decamers as cargo.
> - **Raw data:** EMPIAR-10716 (multi-frame TIFF micrographs, 8,109 movies, 40 frames, 0.326 Å
>   super-resolution pixel, gain reference `gain.dm4`).
> - **Deposited results:** EMD-12853 (icosahedral encapsulin map, 2.5 Å) · PDB 7ODW.
> - **Symmetry:** Encapsulin shell = icosahedral (**I**). Ferritin cargo (EncFtn decamer) = **D5**,
>   recovered by custom non-point-group symmetry expansion.
> - **Source URL:** https://guide.cryosparc.com/processing-data/tutorials-and-case-studies/case-study-end-to-end-processing-of-encapsulated-ferritin-empiar-10716
> - **Dataset citation:** Ross J, Baslé A, Clarke DJ, Marles-Wright J. *Haliangium ochraceum*
>   encapsulin : encapsulated ferritin. EMPIAR-10716 / EMD-12853 / PDB 7ODW (2021–2022).
> - **Aim (per the guide):** demonstrate advanced cryoSPARC tools for structures with unconventional
>   symmetry — high-symmetry ab-initio reconstruction, local symmetry, non-point-group symmetry,
>   symmetry expansion, and custom geometry operations.

---

## Overview of the workflow

The case study has two halves:

- **Section A — Encapsulin shell:** import + motion/CTF in CryoSPARC Live → blob pick → 2D → ab-initio
  (C1) → symmetry alignment to **I** → homogeneous refinement with symmetry relaxation → enforce **I** via
  Homogeneous Reconstruction Only → global CTF refine → particle subtraction (remove the shell).
- **Section B — Encapsulated ferritin (EncFtn) cargo:** working from the subtracted particles, re-align
  onto the internal tetrahedron of four EncFtn decamers, perform a **custom (non-point-group) symmetry
  expansion** over the four cargo positions, classify, then **D5** local refinement of the cargo.

Final resolutions reported by the guide:

| Map | Symmetry | Resolution |
|---|---|---|
| Encapsulin shell (consensus, C1 refinement) | C1 | ~3.0 Å |
| Encapsulin shell (symmetry enforced) | I | **2.5 Å** |
| Encapsulated ferritin cargo (local refinement) | D5 | **~2.8 Å** (vs. 5–6 Å published) |

---

## SECTION A — Encapsulin shell

### A1. Preprocessing & particle picking (CryoSPARC Live)

**Live session configuration**

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Raw pixel size | 0.326 Å (super-resolution) |
| Accelerating voltage | 300 kV |
| Spherical aberration (Cs) | 2.7 mm |
| Total exposure dose | 40.509 e⁻/Å² |
| Output F-crop factor | 0.5 (→ effective 0.652 Å pixel) |
| Save results in 16-bit floating point | Yes |
| Gain reference | `gain.dm4` (EMPIAR `data/micrographs/gain.dm4`) |

Motion correction and CTF estimation run inside CryoSPARC Live (Patch Motion Correction + Patch CTF
Estimation) as movies stream in.

**Blob particle picking**

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Minimum particle diameter | 160 Å |
| Maximum particle diameter | 230 Å |
| Use circular blob | Yes |
| Use ring blob | Yes |

**Extraction**

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Extraction box size | 800 px |
| Fourier crop to box size | 512 px |

(Extracting at 800 px and Fourier-cropping to 512 px keeps a generous box for the large ~200 Å shell
while binning the super-resolution data to a working 0.652 Å pixel.)

**CTF / curation in CryoSPARC Live**

- Upper CTF fit resolution threshold: **6 Å** (set in the Overview tab).
- Adjust the **Normalized Cross-Correlation (NCC)** and **Power** score sliders to remove false-positive
  picks before exporting particles.

> Dataset note: the case study processes **2,815 movies** (a subset of the 8,109 total) through Live.

### A2. 2D Classification

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Number of classes | 80 |
| Minimum separation distance | 60 Å |
| Number of GPUs to parallelize | 3 |

**Selection criteria:** keep classes showing high-resolution encapsulin detail; reject overlapping
particles, empty classes, ice/carbon edges, and junk.

### A3. Ab-initio reconstruction (asymmetric)

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Maximum resolution | 8 Å |
| Initial resolution | 25 Å |
| Center structures in real space | Off |
| Enforce non-negativity | Off |
| Symmetry | C1 |

Run **asymmetric (C1)** so the internal tetrahedral EncFtn arrangement is preserved (not averaged away by
imposing I too early).

### A4. Symmetry alignment to icosahedral (Volume Alignment Tools)

- Activate **symmetry alignment**.
- Symmetry string: **`I`** (icosahedral).

This aligns the C1 ab-initio volume onto the icosahedral symmetry axes so that a subsequent symmetric
refinement/reconstruction is correctly registered.

### A5. Homogeneous Refinement (with symmetry relaxation)

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Symmetry | I |
| Symmetry relaxation method | maximization |
| Dynamic mask start resolution | 1 Å |

> Guide wording: *"Setting the symmetry relaxation to 'maximization' enables symmetry relaxation. It can
> also be set to 'marginalization', which uses a slightly different method for finding the optimal
> pose."* Symmetry relaxation lets the refinement apply the overall symmetry constraint while preserving
> asymmetric internal detail.

Result: ~**3.0 Å** C1-aligned refinement with ~250k particles.

### A6. Enforce I via Homogeneous Reconstruction Only

> Guide wording: *"To get a icosahedrally (I) symmetric reference for subtracting the encapsulin away,
> we don't have to repeat a full refinement. Instead, connect the particles from the previous C1
> refinement to a Homogeneous Reconstruction Only job, and run the job with a symmetry of I specified."*

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Symmetry | I (enforced) |
| Particles | retain C1 alignments from the refinement above |

Result: **2.5 Å** icosahedral encapsulin map (the EMD-12853 deposit-equivalent).

### A7. Mask generation (Volume Tools)

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Type of input volume | map |
| Type of output volume | mask |
| Threshold | user-selected (preserve the encapsulin shell) |
| Dilation radius | 4 px |
| Soft padding width | 18 px |

### A8. Global CTF Refinement

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Fit anisotropic magnification | Yes |
| Iterations | 2 |
| Inputs | particles + volume (from the symmetric Reconstruction Only) + mask |

> Guide wording: *"Connect the particles and volume from the upstream symmetry-enforced Reconstruction
> Only to a Global CTF Refinement job… Activate 'Fit anisotropic mag', to allow for estimation of
> anisotropic magnification."*

Then re-run **Homogeneous Reconstruction Only (symmetry I)** using the Global-CTF-Refinement output
particles to produce the post-CTF-refined map.

### A9. Particle subtraction (remove the shell)

- Inputs: particles, the I-symmetric volume, and the encapsulin-covering mask.
- Effect: subtracts the encapsulin shell signal, leaving the internal EncFtn cargo density in the
  subtracted particle stack — the input to Section B.

---

## SECTION B — Encapsulated ferritin (EncFtn) cargo

> Demonstration (unsuccessful, shown for instruction): a naive Homogeneous Reconstruction of the
> subtracted particles gives ~10 Å; a Homogeneous Refinement (dynamic mask start 1 Å) stalls at ~6.9 Å
> with overfitting artefacts. The cargo needs the symmetry-expansion treatment below.

### B1. Group re-alignment on the tetrahedron

**Spherical mask:** create a soft sphere centered at the box center (made with the UCSF ChimeraX *Map
Eraser* tool), import into cryoSPARC as a mask, then pad with **Volume Tools**:

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Type input / output | mask / mask |
| Threshold | 0.5 |
| Soft padding width | 20 px |

**3D Classification**

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Number of classes | 20 |
| Filter resolution | 8 Å |
| O-EM batch size per class | 2000 |
| O-EM learning rate init | 0.9 |
| O-EM learning rate half-life | 0% |
| Force hard classification | On |
| Solvent mask | spherical mask |

**Align 3D Maps**

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Update particle alignments | On |
| Reference map | best-resolved 3D class |
| Reference mask | spherical mask |
| Inputs | all 20 volumes + all particles from the 3D Classification |

Then **Homogeneous Reconstruction Only** (particles from Align 3D Maps, spherical mask) for a consensus
post-alignment structure.

### B2. Custom symmetry expansion (non-point-group symmetry)

The four EncFtn decamers sit at tetrahedron vertices inside the shell — there is no single point group
that captures this, so the case study builds a **custom symmetry expansion** over the four cargo
positions.

**Mask bases (UCSF ChimeraX):** create **4** mask bases (one per EncFtn unit) with the *Segment Map*
tool — group by connectivity and adjust the threshold until exactly 4 disconnected discs appear.

**Import 3D Volumes**

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Wildcard path | `/path/to/directory/encftn_maskbase*.mrc` |
| Type | mask |
| Output | 4 imported mask bases |

**Volume Tools (×4, one per mask)**

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Type input / output | mask / mask |
| Threshold | user-selected |
| Dilation radius | 2 px |
| Soft padding width | 16 px |

**Volume Alignment Tools (×4, one per mask)**

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Re-center to mask center of mass | On |
| Reassign UIDs | On |
| Inputs | each mask + volume + particles (from Reconstruction Only) |

(Centers each EncFtn at the box center and generates unique particle IDs so the four copies can be
treated as independent particle groups.)

**Align 3D Maps (superimpose the four copies)**

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Reference volume | one EncFtn (from Volume Alignment Tools) |
| Reference mask | the corresponding mask |
| Maps to align | the 4 EncFtn volumes (from Volume Alignment Tools) |
| Particles | the 4 particle sets |
| Update particle alignments | On |

This rotationally superimposes the four EncFtn copies — the "expansion": one physical particle now
contributes four cargo views.

### B3. Group re-alignment on EncFtn (repeat ×2)

**3D Classification (iterations 1 & 2)**

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Number of classes | 20 |
| Filter resolution | 6 Å |
| O-EM batch size per class | 2000 |
| O-EM learning rate init | 1 |
| O-EM learning rate half-life | 0% |
| Force hard classification | On |
| Solvent mask | mask covering one EncFtn |
| Inputs | the 4 particle groups (Particles for map {0,1,2,3}) |

**Volume Alignment Tools (D5 symmetry alignment)**

- Select the class with the strongest 5-fold symmetry.
- Do symmetry alignment: **On**.
- Symmetry string: **`D5`** (the EncFtn decamer is a D5 dimer-of-pentamers).

**Align 3D Maps**

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Update particle alignments | On |
| Maps to align | all volumes from the 3D Classification |
| Particles | all particles from the 3D Classification |
| Reference map | the D5-aligned volume (from Volume Alignment Tools) |
| Reference mask | corresponding mask |

### B4. Local refinement (D5)

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Use pose/shift Gaussian prior during alignment | On |
| Std. dev. of prior over rotation | 6° |
| Std. dev. of prior over shifts | 3 Å |
| Re-center rotations each iteration | On |
| Re-center shifts each iteration | On |
| Symmetry | D5 |
| Number of extra final passes | 0 |

**Inputs**

- Particles: the selected high-quality classes (from Align 3D Maps).
- Initial volume: from the upstream Volume Alignment Tools.
- Static mask: from the upstream Volume Alignment Tools.

**Particle selection:** retained ~445k of ~1,009k particles (selected classes only).

**Final result:** **~2.8 Å** for the encapsulated ferritin cargo (vs. 5–6 Å in the published structure).

---

## Key numbers for the importer / downloader

| Field | Value | Source |
|---|---|---|
| Raw (super-res) pixel | 0.326 Å | EMPIAR-10716 imageset header / Live config |
| Binned (physical) pixel | 0.652 Å | EMDB EMD-12853 (= 0.326 × 2 via F-crop 0.5) |
| Voltage | 300 kV | EMDB / Live config |
| Cs | 2.7 mm | cryoSPARC case study Live config (NOT in EMDB API) |
| Total dose | 40.509 e⁻/Å² | EMDB / Live config |
| Frames per movie | 40 | EMPIAR imageset header |
| Box / F-crop | 800 px → 512 px | case study extraction |
| Gain reference | `gain.dm4` | EMPIAR `data/micrographs/gain.dm4` |
| Movie format | multi-frame TIFF (`*_fractions.tiff`) | EMPIAR FTP listing |

## Symmetry summary

- **Encapsulin shell:** impose **I** only after a C1 ab-initio + C1 refinement; obtain the I map via
  Homogeneous Reconstruction Only (symmetry I). The deposit EMD-12853 / PDB 7ODW is the I shell at 2.5 Å.
- **EncFtn cargo:** **D5**, reached by particle subtraction of the shell + custom non-point-group
  symmetry expansion over the four tetrahedrally-arranged decamers + D5 local refinement (~2.8 Å). This
  cargo map is the "breadth" demonstration; it is not the EMD-12853 deposit (which is the I shell).
literature.md easy how this structure was actually reconstructed in the associated publication, plus distilled guidance for this run · 9,412 chars
# Encapsulin + ferritin cargo (EMPIAR-10716) — I shell + D5 cargo — literature review

_How this structure was actually reconstructed in the associated publication / deposit, behind the deposited EMD-12853 / 7ODW map. This is the **literature** layer — a factual account of the real workflow, distinct from the generic tutorial / case-study recipe. The **review** below is provided in the easy and medium variants; the **additional instructions** (after the marker) only in easy._

> Provenance: compiled from the associated publication + the EMDB / EMPIAR deposition metadata, with adversarial verification of every numeric claim against primary sources. A dated snapshot — not maintained.

## How the authors actually reconstructed *Haliangium ochraceum* encapsulin (Ross et al. 2022)

The deposited structures for this environment come from Ross et al., "Pore dynamics and asymmetric cargo loading in an encapsulin nanocompartment," *Sci Adv* 2022;8(4):eabj4461 ([PMC8791618](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC8791618/)). It is important to separate the **authors' real workflow** (described here) from the generic cryoSPARC case study that re-processes the same EMPIAR-10716 movies as a teaching recipe — they differ in software stack, data scope, binning route, and the science they resolve.

**Data collection.** Movies were collected on an FEI Titan Krios (300 kV, field-emission gun) at the Electron Bio-imaging Centre (eBIC), with a Gatan K3 detector in super-resolution counting mode, movies saved as TIFF (digitization 11,520 × 8,184 px) ([EMDB EMD-12853](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-12853); [EMPIAR-10716](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/api/entry/10716/)). Grid screening was performed separately on an FEI F20 (200 kV) at Edinburgh — the 200 kV figure refers only to screening, not the deposited data. Each movie has 40 frames over a 1 s exposure, with an average dose of 40.509 e⁻/Å² ([EMD-12853](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-12853)). 8,109 movies were collected ([EMPIAR-10716](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/empiar/api/entry/10716/)). The raw super-resolution pixel is 0.326 Å; the working/deposited pixel is 0.652 Å. Defocus was collected over 0.7–2.5 μm in 0.3 μm steps (Supplementary Table S2, freely accessible via the open-access [PMC8791618 supplement](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/europepmc/webservices/rest/PMC8791618/supplementaryFiles)); magnification is not reported in any accessible primary source. Grids were Quantifoil holey-gold (200 mesh, R 2/2), glow-discharged 30 s, with vitrification on an FEI Vitrobot at 8 °C / 100% humidity, plunge-frozen in liquid ethane ([PMC8791618](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC8791618/)).

**The deposited shell (the main reconstruction) was done in RELION 3.1, not cryoSPARC.** The paper states verbatim, "Processing steps for the main reconstruction were performed with the Relion3.1 software package," and the [EMD-12853](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-12853) header independently attributes the deposited 2.5 Å map to RELION 3.1 ([PMC8791618](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC8791618/)). The authors' pipeline: super-resolution movies were binned 2×2 and motion-corrected with MotionCor2 (this 2×2 binning is the route that yields the 0.652 Å working pixel — distinct from the case study's F-crop 0.5); defocus determined by CTFFIND4, with poor CTF fits and bad ice manually discarded. Note: the paper specifies no explicit dose-weighting flag, so whether dose-weighting was applied is indeterminate from the text (MotionCor2 does not dose-weight by default). Particles were template-autopicked in RELION 3.1 ("A template for autopicking was created using 2D classes from manually picked particles") and extracted at a 512 px box. The deposit records 340,403 particles selected upstream ([EMD-12853](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-12853)).

**Classification, refinement, and symmetry.** Three rounds of 2D classification removed bad particles (the intermediate post-2D count is not separately reported in accessible sources). 3D classes were generated **both with and without icosahedral symmetry imposed ("I1" and "C1")**, and the best class from each was taken forward — this dual-symmetry strategy is what let the authors detect the internal cargo rather than averaging it away. For the shell, the best 3D class went through 3D refinement → CTF refinement → further 3D refinement → Bayesian polishing → a final 3D refinement → postprocessing with a soft spherical mask, with local resolution estimated in RELION 3.1. The deposited icosahedral shell map ([EMD-12853](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-12853), PDB [7ODW](https://www.rcsb.org/structure/7ODW)) reached **2.5 Å** by gold-standard FSC at 0.143, using 254,134 particles (point group I, 576³ box, 0.652 Å/px, overall sharpening B-factor 86.0 Å²). The atomic model was built from a Phyre homology model (template 3DKT) docked in Chimera, real-space refined in PHENIX 1.18, and manually built in Coot.

**The cargo / asymmetry branch — the paper's actual science.** The whole-complex asymmetric (C1) reconstruction is deposited as [EMD-12873](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-12873) at **3.5 Å** with 68,096 particles (the paper text quotes ~3.7 Å — a minor deposit-vs-text discrepancy). The EncFtn cargo was characterized by exporting particles to **cryoSPARC** for 3DVA and, in RELION 3.1, by symmetry expansion of the I particle set followed by masked 3D classification without alignment centered on a vertex, separating **open vs closed pentamer pore states**. These yielded the symmetry-expanded pentamer maps [EMD-12864](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-12864) (open, 2.64 Å, B = 11.34) and [EMD-12859](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-12859) (closed, 2.4 Å, B = 86.0), both C1 at FSC 0.143 ([EMD-12853](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-12853); EMDB headers). The cargo decamer itself has no separate deposited EMDB map. The headline findings — pore open/closed dynamics and asymmetric cargo loading — are the authors' own and are **not** reproduced by the generic case-study recipe.

## Additional instructions (distilled for this run)

Prescriptive guidance for rebuilding the **encapsulin shell** map (EMD-12853, 2.5 Å) from EMPIAR-10716 movies in cryoSPARC. This follows the case-study recipe, which is the runnable path for the easy environment.

**Import / pixel / gain**
- These are **super-resolution K3** movies. Import at the raw super-res pixel **0.326 Å**, NOT the physical 0.652 Å. Getting this wrong corrupts every downstream Å-based parameter.
- Set Fourier-crop factor **0.5** at extraction → working pixel **0.652 Å** (matches the deposit). The authors' RELION route instead binned 2×2 in MotionCor2; in cryoSPARC use F-crop, not super-res binning.
- Acquisition: voltage **300 kV**, Cs **2.7 mm** (from the case-study Live config — not in the EMDB/EMPIAR API), total dose **40.509 e⁻/Å²** over **40 frames**, multi-frame TIFF.
- Gain: one reference, `gain.dm4` (Gatan DM4, ~360 MB) at `data/micrographs/gain.dm4`. cryoSPARC reads .dm4 natively — no conversion. There is ONE gain and effectively one session; the per-GridSquare folders are spatial tiling, so no multi-session gain merging. cryoSPARC matches the super-res gain dimensions to the movie internally.
- Run Patch Motion Correction + Patch CTF (cryoSPARC Live).

**Symmetry decision (the crux of this dataset)**
- The shell is icosahedral (point group **I**, T=1, 60 subunits), but it packages four D5 EncFtn decamers in a tetrahedral arrangement. Do **NOT** impose I too early — it would average away the internal cargo.
- Correct strategy: **ab-initio in C1** → Volume Alignment Tools to symmetry-align the C1 volume to **I** → Homogeneous Refinement with symmetry I + symmetry relaxation (method "maximization") → enforce I cleanly via **Homogeneous Reconstruction Only** with symmetry I on the C1-aligned particles. This gives the 2.5 Å I shell.
- (Cargo is out of scope for the easy map but reachable via shell particle subtraction + custom non-point-group symmetry expansion over the 4 tetrahedral EncFtn positions + D5 local refinement. No separate cargo EMDB map exists.)

**Picking, box, yield**
- Blob picker tuned to the ~200–240 Å shell (case study: min 160 Å / max 230 Å diameter). Extract at **800 px box, Fourier-crop to 512 px**.
- Expected particle yield: on the case-study **2,815-movie subset**, ~250k particles into the I shell refinement. On the **full 8,109-movie** dataset the deposit used 254,134 particles in the final reconstruction (from 340,403 selected). Expect order ~250k–340k shell particles.

**Sharpening / refinement detail**
- Before the final I reconstruction, run Global CTF Refinement (fit anisotropic magnification, 2 iterations) to tighten resolution.
- Refinement/CTF mask: Volume Tools, dilation 4 px, soft padding 18 px.
- Standard auto B-factor sharpening; the deposit's overall B is 86.0 Å². No unusual sharpening.

**What "good" looks like**
- Final I shell map at **~2.5 Å** by gold-standard FSC 0.143, in a 576³ box at 0.652 Å/px (box edge ~375.6 Å), wrong-handedness corrected. Crisp icosahedral shell with resolved side-chain detail. Place against deposited EMD-12853 / PDB 7ODW. If your map sits at the physical pixel by mistake (0.652 imported as raw), resolution and scale will be self-consistent but wrong — cross-check box-edge Å and particle diameter.
cryosparc-tools-api.md easy/medium/hard the cryosparc-tools API you drive cryoSPARC with · 2,885 chars
# cryosparc-tools API notes (public; tools.cryosparc.com)

> Shared, dataset-agnostic context file. Staged into `REFS_DIR` for every rollout variant and read by the
> agent at run time. The numbers/parameters specific to a dataset are NOT here — they live in `acquisition.md`
> (the told-facts) and, where provided, the processing `tutorial.md` / `literature.md`.

You operate cryoSPARC by writing Python with the `cryosparc-tools` package (public docs: tools.cryosparc.com).
The connection and a project are already set up — see `working-environment.md` for what is pre-bound. Key API:

- DISCOVER the available job types: `cs.print_job_types()` prints every job type — its category, its builder
  TYPE STRING (the string you pass to create_job), and its GUI title (the names a tutorial uses). You can
  filter by category, e.g. `cs.print_job_types("particle_picking")`. This is how you map a processing step to
  the right job-type string.
- CREATE + wire a job:
      job = cs.create_job(project_uid, workspace, "<type_string>",
                          connections={"<input_group>": (source_job_uid, "<source_output_group>"), ...},
                          params={"<param>": value, ...}, title="...")
  After `job.refresh()`, introspect the job to learn its exact input groups, output groups, and parameters
  (names + current/default values) so you know what to wire and what to set:
      spec = job.model.model_dump()["spec"]
      spec["inputs"].keys()    # input-group names to wire INTO
      spec["outputs"].keys()   # output-group names to wire FROM (and to load)
      spec["params"]           # all parameters with their current values
  You can also set a parameter after creation with `job.set_param(name, value)`. Build jobs in dependency order.
- RUN a job: `job.queue(lane=...)` then `status = job.wait_for_done(timeout=..., error_on_incomplete=False)`
  (returns the status string; if it times out the server keeps running it — poll again, don't block unbounded).
  Compute lanes are `LANE_CPU` and `LANE_GPU`; lightweight / interactive jobs run on the master node with
  `lane=None`. Output row counts: `len(job.load_output("<output_group>"))`.
- INTERACTIVE jobs: some jobs pause in a `"waiting"` state when queued (they expect interactive input) rather
  than completing. Drive such a job headlessly via `job.interact(action, body)` and then finalize it, or
  achieve the equivalent curation programmatically from the relevant outputs — your choice. (A `"waiting"`
  job is not `"completed"`; don't `wait_for_done` on it expecting completion.)
- RESULTS: a finished refinement/volume job carries its resolution + diagnostics in its model, at
  `job.model.model_dump()["spec"]["outputs"]["<group>"]["latest_summary_stats"]` (e.g. gold-standard FSC
  resolutions in Å and the Guinier B-factor). You can also `load_output` any result and read MRC maps off disk.
working-environment.md easy/medium/hard the objects and inspection helpers pre-bound in your namespace · 1,785 chars
# Your working environment

> Shared, dataset-agnostic context file. Staged into `REFS_DIR` for every rollout variant and read by the
> agent at run time. It describes the namespace and helpers you act through; it does NOT contain any
> dataset-specific facts.

You write code through one tool, `run_python(code)`, which executes it in a PERSISTENT Python namespace on the
lab workstation and returns stdout + the value of the last expression + any traceback — so you iterate like a
real coder: write a small block, read the result/error, fix, continue.

Pre-bound (do NOT reconnect or create a project/workspace):

- `cs` — a connected cryosparc-tools client
- `project`, `project_uid`, `project_dir` — the target project (already created)
- `workspace` — a fresh EMPTY workspace; build everything here
- `DATA_DIR` — the dataset directory; the raw movies are under it (see `acquisition.md` for the glob)
- `REFS_DIR` — the directory holding the reference materials staged for this run (this file and the others
  named in your brief). Read them with e.g. `print(open(os.path.join(REFS_DIR, "acquisition.md")).read())`.
- `LANE_CPU` / `LANE_GPU` — the compute lanes to queue jobs onto
- `np`, `os`, `json`, `time`, and `find_job(uid)`

To inspect intermediate results, lab visualization utilities are available and return images you can see:

- `show_class_montage(job)` — 2D class averages, labelled by class index
- `show_picks(job, cut=None)` — pick score distribution + picks drawn on micrographs; pass
  `cut=(ncc, power_min, power_max)` to colour kept vs rejected
- `show_volume(job)` — map orthoslices
- `show_mask_sweep(job)` — mask-threshold sweep on a low-passed map

You may also load any output and plot your own diagnostics. Use whatever you need to make your judgments.

**Classification, refinement, and symmetry.** Three rounds of 2D classification removed bad particles (the intermediate post-2D count is not separately reported in accessible sources). 3D classes were generated **both with and without icosahedral symmetry imposed ("I1" and "C1")**, and the best class from each was taken forward — this dual-symmetry strategy is what let the authors detect the internal cargo rather than averaging it away. For the shell, the best 3D class went through 3D refinement → CTF refinement → further 3D refinement → Bayesian polishing → a final 3D refinement → postprocessing with a soft spherical mask, with local resolution estimated in RELION 3.1. The deposited icosahedral shell map ([EMD-12853](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-12853), PDB [7ODW](https://www.rcsb.org/structure/7ODW)) reached **2.5 Å** by gold-standard FSC at 0.143, using 254,134 particles (point group I, 576³ box, 0.652 Å/px, overall sharpening B-factor 86.0 Å²). The atomic model was built from a Phyre homology model (template 3DKT) docked in Chimera, real-space refined in PHENIX 1.18, and manually built in Coot.

**The cargo / asymmetry branch — the paper's actual science.** The whole-complex asymmetric (C1) reconstruction is deposited as [EMD-12873](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-12873) at **3.5 Å** with 68,096 particles (the paper text quotes ~3.7 Å — a minor deposit-vs-text discrepancy). The EncFtn cargo was characterized by exporting particles to **cryoSPARC** for 3DVA and, in RELION 3.1, by symmetry expansion of the I particle set followed by masked 3D classification without alignment centered on a vertex, separating **open vs closed pentamer pore states**. These yielded the symmetry-expanded pentamer maps [EMD-12864](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-12864) (open, 2.64 Å, B = 11.34) and [EMD-12859](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-12859) (closed, 2.4 Å, B = 86.0), both C1 at FSC 0.143 ([EMD-12853](https://www.ebi.ac.uk/emdb/api/entry/EMD-12853); EMDB headers). The cargo decamer itself has no separate deposited EMDB map. The headline findings — pore open/closed dynamics and asymmetric cargo loading — are the authors' own and are **not** reproduced by the generic case-study recipe.
acquisition.md hard what's physically on the workstation — the data location and the microscope basics; everything else you work out · 583 chars
# What's on the workstation — Encapsulin + ferritin cargo (EMPIAR-10716) — I shell + D5 cargo

- A gain reference `gain.dm4` is present in `DATA_DIR`.
- Acquisition: FEI Titan Krios (300 kV); 300 kV, Cs 2.7 mm.

System prompt
You are a senior computational structural biologist working autonomously in a cryo-EM lab. Your PI has handed you a dataset and a goal and expects you to carry out the reconstruction end-to-end using your OWN scientific judgment — you choose the workflow, the jobs, every parameter, and every particle/class/mask curation decision yourself. Your objective on every run is to produce the best reconstruction the data can support — always push for the highest-quality map achievable, and treat any published or reference result as a guide and a floor to aim past, not a ceiling to stop at. You operate cryoSPARC entirely programmatically by writing Python with the cryosparc-tools API, through one tool, run_python, that executes your code in a persistent namespace on the workstation and returns stdout, the last expression's value, and any traceback — so you work iteratively: write a little code, read the result or error, fix, continue. You are unattended: be decisive, never ask questions, debug from tracebacks yourself, and keep going until the goal is met. The cryoSPARC connection, the project, and a fresh empty workspace are already set up and pre-bound — do not reconnect or create a project/workspace; do all your work in the pre-bound workspace. When you have produced and validated the final result, call finish.
Task message — slim brief + file manifest
From: your PI
Subject: Encapsulin + ferritin cargo (EMPIAR-10716) — I shell + D5 cargo — reconstruction

We have a raw cryo-EM movie dataset of Haliangium ochraceum encapsulin nanocompartment + EncFtn cargo, I shell + D5 cargo, already on the workstation in DATA_DIR (the EMPIAR-10716 raw movies). The Haliangium ochraceum encapsulin is a ~24 nm icosahedral (T=1, 60-subunit) protein nanocompartment that packages four encapsulated-ferritin (EncFtn) decamers as cargo. The shell has icosahedral (I) symmetry and refines to 2.5 Å (EMD-12853 / 7ODW); each internal cargo decamer has D5 symmetry. A large, high-contrast assembly.

I'd like you to take it all the way to a refined, sharpened high-resolution 3D density map: run the full single-particle analysis pipeline from raw movies onward. Reproduce the established approach for this specimen using your own judgment — I'm not going to spell out every job or parameter; you know single-particle processing, and I've staged a processing tutorial and a review of how this structure was reconstructed in the literature for you to work from. Note: that case study is one documented route to this structure — a guiding framework, not necessarily the optimal recipe for your data and cryoSPARC version. Follow it for orientation, but make your own decisions at every step; the goal is always the best reconstruction this data supports. Drive everything programmatically through cryosparc-tools (no GUI); make every parameter and every particle/class/mask curation call yourself, push for the best reconstruction the data supports (the published map reaches ~2.5 Å), and validate the result with a gold-standard FSC; show me the final map's resolution when you're finished.

I've staged the reference materials for this run in `REFS_DIR` — read each one (they're short) before you start, e.g.:
    import os; print(open(os.path.join(REFS_DIR, "acquisition.md")).read())

- `acquisition.md` — the acquisition facts and sample identity you need to import the movies and set up processing.

- `cryosparc-tools-api.md` — the cryosparc-tools API you drive cryoSPARC with.
- `working-environment.md` — the objects and inspection helpers pre-bound in your namespace.

Proceed now, autonomously, using your own judgment for every decision. When you've reached and validated a final sharpened map, call finish with the resolution.
